# Phase batches

Batch ledger for Garmin Coach v1. A batch is shipped only after `/closeout`
finishes; until then leave the row unstruck. When shipped, strike through the
batch title and set the status to `Shipped`.

Tier map from `DECISIONS.md` #19:

| Tier | Work | Claude | Codex |
|---|---|---|---|
| 🔴 High | Complex reasoning: data-model boundaries, scheduler/sync edge cases, analysis-engine prompts, verdict logic, debugging | Opus | GPT-5.5 |
| 🟢 Mid | Well-specified implementation: CRUD, components, migrations, tests, mechanical refactors | Sonnet | GPT-5.4 |

## v1 batch plan

| Batch | Tier | Status | Phases | Goal | Acceptance criteria |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| ~~Batch 1 — Data model + profile seed~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 1.1 Data-shape audit from `~/garmin-spike/out/` and `~/garmin-spike/out_hive/`.<br>1.2 Alembic/SQLAlchemy model for `users`, `daily_metrics`, `sleep`, `activities`, `activity_timeseries`, `temperature_readings`, `weather_daily`, `manual_entries`, `planned_workouts`, `plan_blocks`, `analyses`, `experiments`, `knowledge_base`.<br>1.3 Shared Zod/TS schemas for the v1 stored shapes.<br>1.4 Seed Mark's admin profile directly in DB. | Replace the old football skeleton with a real Garmin Coach storage foundation and a private seeded user. | Models/migration are derived from the real spike JSON, not old football tables; snake_case DB and camelCase JSON conventions hold; UTC `*_utc` columns and user IANA timezone exist; Mark can log in after direct seed; tests cover migration/model serialization and auth/profile seed path; backend pytest, ruff, mypy pass. |
| ~~Batch 2 — Garmin sync foundation~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 2.1 Store Garmin credential reference/token-cache strategy without committing secrets.<br>2.2 Implement Garmin client service around `garminconnect`/garth using spike fields.<br>2.3 Sync daily metrics, sleep, body battery, HRV, RHR, weight/VO2 and activity summaries.<br>2.4 Sync activity details/time-series including power, HR, cadence, respiration, Performance Condition and Stamina. | Pull Garmin data into the v1 model with idempotent, testable service boundaries. | Service parses representative files including `training_readiness.json`, `sleep.json`, `hrv.json`, `body_battery.json`, `activities.json`, `activity_details.json`, `activity_metric_channels.json`; `recoveryTime` is stored as minutes; repeated syncs upsert without duplicates; secrets stay out of repo/logs; tests cover fixture parsing, idempotency, and failure handling; backend pytest, ruff, mypy pass. |
| ~~Batch 3 — Hive + weather syncs~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 3.1 Implement Hive client wrapper around sync `pyhiveapi` re-login.<br>3.2 Persist live indoor temperature readings from `getAll()` product/device shapes.<br>3.3 Implement Open-Meteo service for Kilmarnock weather daily history/forecast.<br>3.4 Add scheduler jobs for Hive polling and morning weather sync without triggering analysis yet. | Bring the environmental context into the database on the cadence the product needs. | Hive parsing is based on `~/garmin-spike/out_hive/getAll.json`, `getDevices.json`, and `getProducts.json`; indoor temperature reads `parsed[i].props.temperature`; weather uses lat `55.6045`, long `-4.5249`, `wind_speed_unit=mph`, and captures daily high/low plus overnight low/wind; jobs are idempotent and timezone-aware; tests cover parser fixtures, scheduler registration, retries, and no-secret logging; backend pytest, ruff, mypy pass. |
| ~~Batch 4 — 84-night backfill + baselines~~ | 🟢 Mid | Shipped | 4.1 Add one-shot import tooling for `12 Weeks Sleep Data` xlsx, 24 Mar-15 Jun.<br>4.2 Backfill `sleep` and `daily_metrics` from the spreadsheet.<br>4.3 Compute/store baseline helpers used by morning analysis.<br>4.4 Add admin-safe rerun/dry-run behaviour. | Seed the historical sleep/recovery baseline that makes the coach smarter than a one-day read. | Import trusts all spreadsheet columns except the broken constant `Duration`; dates map to the correct user timezone and UTC storage; reruns are idempotent; baselines are reproducible from the 84-night history and exclude known unreliable periods where appropriate; dry-run summarizes intended writes; tests cover parsing, ignored Duration, idempotency, and baseline calculations; backend pytest, ruff, mypy pass. |
| ~~Batch 5 — Training plan + knowledge base~~ | 🟢 Mid | Shipped | 5.1 Store editable knowledge-base sections from `ARCHITECTURE.md` §3.<br>5.2 Ingest current structured training plan and plan blocks.<br>5.3 Add per-day planned-workout override path with version history.<br>5.4 Add internal API/admin UI surfaces for viewing/editing retained state. | Give the app the persistent context his handover docs used to provide. | KB includes profile, data-quality rules, age-adjustment, sleep protocol, active hypotheses, and plan context; planned workouts are structured and versioned, including VO2-session revision support; per-day overrides preserve prior versions; APIs use the standard envelope; tests cover CRUD/versioning and data-quality rule persistence; backend and frontend tests/build/lint pass for touched surfaces. |
| ~~Batch 6 — Morning analysis engine~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 6.1 Build context-packet assembler from KB, daily data, baselines, environment, manual entries, and today's full plan.<br>6.2 Implement Claude call boundary with stored prompt/version metadata.<br>6.3 Encode Green/Amber/Red verdict framework and output rules.<br>6.4 Trigger morning analysis from the 06:30 local sync path and store the result. | Generate the daily morning verdict that replaces the manual Copilot handover loop. | Analysis packet includes the metrics-vs-baselines table, thermal/environment review, plan-aware cycling + strength verdict, age-adjusted sleep, and data-quality guardrails; Red never recommends VO2; Low Garmin readiness can be reconciled as load-driven only when recovery signals justify it; Claude outputs are stored in `analyses`; prompt/version is inspectable; tests cover packet assembly, verdict edge cases, no-balance rule, and stored output; backend pytest, ruff, mypy pass. |
| ~~Batch 7 — Daily app loop surfaces~~ | 🟢 Mid | Shipped | 7.1 Dashboard for today's morning verdict, key metrics, plan, and thermal state.<br>7.2 Manual check-in for BP, subjective score, RPE, feel, supplements, and food.<br>7.3 Adherence capture: did he do the planned work, and what changed?<br>7.4 Data-quality guardian warnings in the UI/API. | Make the daily loop usable from the phone without needing direct DB access. | Mark can open the PWA and see today's verdict/plan/status; manual entries persist and feed later analyses; adherence is captured against the planned workout/version; data-quality warnings prevent L/R balance, bad SpO2/HRV windows, wrist-HR strength recovery, and broken Duration from leaking into decisions; tests cover API and UI flows; frontend build/test/lint and backend pytest/ruff/mypy pass. |
| ~~Batch 8 — Post-workout analysis~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 8.1 Detect newly synced rides from hourly Garmin activity polling.<br>8.2 Assemble post-workout context from activity summary, zones, PC/stamina/time-series, plan, and morning verdict.<br>8.3 Generate/store Claude post-workout analysis.<br>8.4 Surface guided recovery protocol and tomorrow impact. | Close the loop after rides with performance read, recovery guidance, and next-day implications. | New rides trigger once, not repeatedly; strength sessions using wrist HR are excluded from recovery decisions; analysis includes power/HR/zones/cadence/Performance Condition/Stamina/Training Effect where present; output gives a workout rating, specific timed recovery protocol, and tomorrow impact; tests cover trigger idempotency, context assembly, and stored output; backend pytest, ruff, mypy pass. |
| ~~Batch 9 — Nudges + thermal monitoring~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 9.1 Evening nudge scheduler and notification copy for sleep protocol.<br>9.2 Thermal monitoring rules for indoor temperature thresholds.<br>9.3 Data-source freshness alerts for missing Garmin/Hive/weather inputs.<br>9.4 PWA push/notification preferences adapted from the inherited infra. | Use the live data to prevent the known sleep failure modes before bedtime. | Evening nudges are daily, timezone-aware, and respect quiet hours/preferences; thermal alerts respond to pre-cool/seal/peak thresholds including >19.5-20°C disruption risk; stale-source alerts distinguish Garmin, Hive, and weather gaps; inherited push infra no longer uses football terminology; tests cover scheduler timing, preference gating, thermal thresholds, and stale-source handling. |
| ~~Batch 10 — v1 hardening + release polish~~ | 🟢 Mid | Shipped | 10.1 End-to-end smoke scripts for the daily loop.<br>10.2 Observability/runbook updates for syncs, analysis, and deploys.<br>10.3 Security/privacy pass for secrets, logs, private-user assumptions, and backups.<br>10.4 Mobile PWA polish for installability and offline-safe daily views. | Make v1 supportable enough for daily use by Mark. | Runbooks describe common sync/analysis failures and recovery; logs expose job health without secrets; backups and env ownership are clear; mobile install path works; offline/freshness states are clear; final backend/frontend test suites and builds pass; production deploy is verified through `/api/v1/health`, app login, and a non-mutating daily-loop smoke check. |

## v2 batch plan

Batch ledger for Garmin Coach v2 — "the coach". Decomposed from `ARCHITECTURE.md`
§6 (v2 roadmap) and `DECISIONS.md` #25–33. Same conventions as v1: a batch is
shipped only after `/closeout` finishes; leave the row unstruck and `Planned`
until started.

**Sequencing rationale.** The **Zwift delivery rail (Batch 12)** is the
foundational dependency for everything else in v2 — executable coaching, dynamic
restructuring, holiday resume, and app-generated blocks all assume the app can
push a structured workout — so it lands first among the substantive batches.
Each later batch delivers its output *through* that rail under the
propose → approve → push contract (Decision #29).

**Phase 1 debt decision.** The Phase 1 retrospective items are scheduled as a
**standalone clean-up Batch 11 first**, ahead of the substantive v2 work. The
driver is the WC2026 "player" → user rename (Decision/debt #3): it touches
`auth.py`, `models/profile.py`, `models/notification.py`, and router error
details, and grows more expensive with every endpoint v2 adds — so it is cheapest
to clear before Batch 12 onward expand the API surface. The smaller items
(ForgotPin flow, dead `email.py`, `score-input.tsx` JSDoc, residual "predictions"
offline-queue refs) ride along in the same batch.

**Production daily-loop gate.** The 2026-06-21 production smoke check proved the
API/auth/daily-loop surface is live for Mark, but the actual daily data loop is
not yet healthy: Mark had to be seeded, the response had today's
`subjectDate=2026-06-21` but `morningAnalysis`, Garmin daily metrics/sleep,
Hive thermal values, weather, and analyses were all empty, and the first
post-seed Hive poll logged `hive temperature poll failed`. Railway production
was also missing the expected data/analysis environment variables
(`GARMIN_EMAIL`, `GARMIN_PASSWORD`, `GARMIN_TOKENSTORE`, `HIVE_EMAIL` /
`HIVE_PASSWORD`, `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`) and logged `environment="development"`
because `ENVIRONMENT=production` was not set. Treat this as the first Batch 12
carry-in before adding new v2 delivery surfaces: production must show real
Garmin + Hive + weather + morning-analysis data for Mark, not just HTTP 200 and
login success.

**Update (2026-06-21 closeout).** Batch 12 shipped the delivery rail, the Garmin
`GARMIN_TOKENSTORE_B64` token-blob auth, and the Anthropic fail-closed validator,
but the strict data gate is still **not** met: production has no Garmin
daily-metrics/sleep sync — `GarminSyncService.sync_daily` is defined (Batch 2)
but has no caller in `src/`, so today's daily metrics + sleep are never synced
and the morning verdict has no readiness/sleep input. The data gate is relocated
to **Batch 18** (DECISIONS #57).

| Batch | Tier | Status | Phases | Goal | Acceptance criteria |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| ~~Batch 11 — Phase 1 debt clean-up~~ | 🟢 Mid | Shipped | 11.1 Remove or replace the broken `ForgotPinPage.tsx` flow (UI says "enter email" + sends `{email}`, but the API expects `{display_name}` and logs the reset token for manual use); update `App.tsx`, `LoginPage.tsx`, `PinResetPage.tsx` to either drop the route or show a plain "contact Craig to reset your PIN" message.<br>11.2 Delete the dead `apps/api/src/services/email.py` service and the unused `resend_api_key` / `EMAIL_FROM` settings.<br>11.3 Rename WC2026 "player" internals to user/profile: `PlayerRole`, `get_current_player`, `CurrentPlayer`, `AdminPlayer` in `auth.py`; `PlayerRole(StrEnum)` in `models/profile.py`; `player_id` columns in `models/notification.py` (with migration); `"Player not found"` HTTP error details in routers.<br>11.4 Fix the `score-input.tsx` line-11 JSDoc and rename the residual "predictions" offline-queue references (`offlineQueue.ts`, `sw.ts`, `score-input.tsx`) to coaching/submission terms. | Clear the catalogued Phase 1 tech debt before v2 grows the codebase and the player→user rename gets more expensive. | PIN-reset no longer claims email or POSTs `{email}` — route is removed or shows contact-Craig copy consistent with Decision #20; `email.py` and the unused email settings are deleted with no remaining imports/references; backend "player" identifiers are renamed to user/profile, `notification` `player_id` columns are migrated, and HTTP error details updated, with no behaviour change to auth or the daily loop; offline-queue + JSDoc "predictions" references renamed; backend pytest/ruff/mypy and frontend test/build/lint pass. |
| ~~Batch 12 — Zwift delivery rail~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 12.0 Resolve the production daily-loop gate from the 2026-06-21 smoke: seed/confirm Mark, set Railway `ENVIRONMENT=production`, Garmin, Hive, and Anthropic vars, let/manual-trigger the relevant jobs, and verify stored rows plus API payload before building v2 on top.<br>12.1 Build a structured-workout intermediate representation from `planned_workouts` (warmup / intervals / cooldown steps with %FTP target, duration, and cadence).<br>12.2 intervals.icu calendar POST client (free API, athlete `i618709`), OUTPUT-only, with secret handling and no activity ingestion via intervals.icu.<br>12.3 Deterministic `.ZWO` export as the no-dependency fallback.<br>12.4 propose → approve → push workflow with nothing written silently; emit cadence-critical reps as individual steps and verify the IntervalsT cadence override on PC Zwift before locking the emit format. | Give the app a validated, approval-gated rail to deliver a structured workout into Zwift — the foundation for all v2 coaching, only after the v1 daily loop is truly producing live data for Mark. | Production daily-loop smoke passes against the Railway API with Mark login and today's response containing non-null Garmin daily metrics/sleep, non-null `morningAnalysis`, non-empty Hive thermal and weather fields, and no scheduler ERROR lines for the same window; Railway env ownership is documented and all required source/analysis vars are set without leaking secrets. A planned workout converts to the structured IR and to both an intervals.icu calendar payload and a deterministic `.ZWO` file; power + timing match the validated end-to-end result (Decision #25); intervals.icu stays OUTPUT-only with ingestion still direct from Garmin (#27); every push is propose → approve → push with no silent writes (#29); cadence-critical reps emit as individual steps and the IntervalsT cadence-override behaviour is documented as verified/unverified on PC (#32); secrets stay out of repo/logs; tests cover IR generation, `.ZWO` determinism, payload shape, and the approval gate; backend pytest/ruff/mypy pass and touched frontend surfaces build/test/lint. |
| ~~Batch 13 — Executable coaching (closed loop)~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 13.1 On an Amber morning verdict, regenerate the adjusted workout (cut duration 20–30%, drop a zone, no HIT) as a structured-workout proposal; Red never produces a VO2 push.<br>13.2 Auto-push approved workouts a couple of days ahead and surface the week-ahead in the UI (Decision #31).<br>13.3 PWA approval surface (propose → approve → push) wired to the Batch 12 rail.<br>13.4 Record every proposal and push in the `analyses` audit log. | Make coaching executable: an Amber morning or restructure regenerates the workout and, on approval, delivers it to Zwift — acted on, not just advised (Decision #30). | An Amber morning (or restructure) produces an adjusted structured workout honouring the verdict framework, and Red never emits VO2; nothing reaches Zwift without explicit approval (#29); approved workouts deliver via the Batch 12 rail, idempotently, and are recorded in `analyses`; the week-ahead is visible in the UI; tests cover Amber-triggered regeneration, the approval gate, idempotent delivery, and audit storage; backend pytest/ruff/mypy and frontend test/build pass. |
| ~~Batch 14 — Dynamic weekly restructuring~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 14.1 Weekly restructure engine that never stacks VO2 + Sweet-Spot on the same/adjacent days, reordering within the week.<br>14.2 Defer-on-fatigue logic driven by recovery signals and verdict trend.<br>14.3 Add Rønnestad 30/15 to the VO2 progression toolkit (build weeks ~Wk7+, ERG off, even-paced ~105–110% FTP / 15 s easy — Decision #33).<br>14.4 Restructure proposals versioned on `planned_workouts` and delivered only via propose → approve → push (Batch 12/13). | Let the plan adapt within the week to fatigue and session-spacing rules instead of running a fixed slate. | The restructurer never schedules VO2 and Sweet-Spot back-to-back; fatigue defers hard sessions based on recovery signals; Rønnestad 30/15 is selectable in the VO2 progression with its documented constraints; restructures are versioned on `planned_workouts` and reach Zwift only on approval; tests cover the no-stack rule, defer-on-fatigue, 30/15 emission, and versioning; backend pytest/ruff/mypy pass. |
| ~~Batch 15 — Holiday pause/resume~~ | 🟢 Mid | Shipped | 15.1 Capture a holiday window (start/end) treated as a recovery-week equivalent.<br>15.2 Correct block continuation on return: pre-holiday Build1→Build2; Build2→repeat Build1.<br>15.3 Versioned plan updates plus a UI surface to pause/resume. | Handle holidays without derailing the 13-week block structure. | A holiday window is treated as a recovery-week equivalent; on return the block continues per the documented rule (Build1→Build2; Build2→repeat Build1); plan changes are versioned and visible in the UI; tests cover both continuation cases and the recovery-equivalent treatment; backend pytest/ruff/mypy and touched frontend surfaces pass. |
| ~~Batch 16 — App-generated 13-week blocks~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 16.1 Conversational generator that produces a 13-week 2121 block from profile/FTP/history.<br>16.2 Refine-then-lock workflow — mould it, fix errors, then lock (Decision #16).<br>16.3 Generated VO2 days use the Batch 14 VO2 progression toolkit (incl. Rønnestad 30/15).<br>16.4 Locked blocks feed the daily loop and deliver via the Zwift rail on approval. | Let the app generate future training blocks the way Mark moulded them by hand, so the plan is never forgotten. | The generator emits a structured, versioned 13-week 2121 block (2 build / 1 recovery / wk12 taper / wk13 consolidation); refine-then-lock preserves edits and locks on confirmation; generated VO2 days can use the 30/15 progression; locked blocks feed the daily loop and the Zwift rail under approval; tests cover generation shape, refine/lock versioning, and progression rules; backend pytest/ruff/mypy and frontend pass. |
| ~~Batch 17 — Monitoring + insight~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 17.1 FTP-drift detection from power/HR trends, with the evidence window surfaced.<br>17.2 Early-warning drift alerts on degrading recovery/HRV/sleep trends ahead of a Red.<br>17.3 Driver/correlation analysis identifying the strongest movers of sleep/recovery from history.<br>17.4 Experiment tracker for active hypotheses (collagen, recovery-week disruption, 04:00 waking) writing to `experiments`/`analyses`. | Turn the accumulated history into proactive insight: drift warnings, correlations, and tracked experiments. | FTP-drift is detected and surfaced with its evidence window; early-warning alerts fire on degrading trends before a Red verdict; driver/correlation analysis identifies the strongest movers of sleep/recovery from the 84-night+ history; the experiment tracker manages active hypotheses with status/outcomes and writes audit rows; tests cover drift detection, alert thresholds, correlation computation, and experiment lifecycle; backend pytest/ruff/mypy pass. |
| ~~Batch 18 — Production daily-loop data sync~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 18.1 Wire `GarminSyncService.sync_daily` into the production scheduler — sync today's daily metrics + sleep (readiness, body battery, HRV, RHR, sleep stages) for active profiles, 429-safe, before the 06:30 morning analysis runs.<br>18.2 Ensure the morning analysis and `/api/v1/daily-loop` then read non-null daily metrics/sleep.<br>18.3 Verify the deferred Batch 12 strict daily-loop smoke passes in production.<br>18.4 Fix production Hive auth so the strict smoke's Hive-thermal field and the "no scheduler ERROR lines" condition can pass: resume from a persisted Cognito refresh token (`HIVE_TOKENSTORE_B64`) because the account requires SMS_MFA, and render scheduler tracebacks (`format_exc_info`) — DECISIONS #59. | Close the production daily-loop data gate deferred from Batch 12 (DECISIONS #57): make the live morning verdict run on real readiness + sleep data, not empty inputs. | A scheduled production job syncs today's Garmin daily metrics + sleep for active profiles idempotently and 429-safely; the 06:30 morning analysis consumes them; the strict `scripts/smoke_daily_loop.py` (`SMOKE_STRICT_DAILY_LOOP=1`) passes against the Railway API with Mark login (non-null daily metrics/sleep, non-null morning analysis, Hive thermal + weather, no scheduler ERROR lines); tests cover the sync wiring and the morning-analysis-with-data path; backend pytest/ruff/mypy pass. |

## v3 batch plan

Batch ledger for Garmin Coach v3 — "the long game". Decomposed from
`ARCHITECTURE.md` §6 (v3 roadmap). Same conventions as v1/v2: a batch is shipped
only after `/closeout` finishes; leave the row unstruck and `Planned` until
started. One batch per v3 roadmap bullet, capstone last. Decision numbers are
assigned at `/batch-start` (next free is #80).

**Narrative reviews use the Claude boundary; rollups stay deterministic.** Unlike
the deterministic engines of Batches 14/16/17 (#63/#69/#71), v3's reviews, the
trends narrative, and the handover export are inherently *narrative*, so they
reuse the thin Anthropic Messages boundary with stored prompt/version metadata in
`analyses` (the Batch 6/8 pattern, #47) — fakeable in tests without
`ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`. The *rollup packets* that feed them stay deterministic and
unit-testable.

**Human/API-triggered, not new scheduler crons.** Following #64/#71, reviews,
trends, and the handover export generate on demand via `POST /…/run` and record to
`analyses`; `GET` previews never write. An optional scheduled `/run` can be layered
on later without changing the engines — no silent background rewriting and no
racing the 06:30 pipeline.

**Migration-free where possible.** Outputs land in `analyses` under new
`analysis_type` values (`weekly_review`, `monthly_review`, `seasonal_trend`,
`experiment_evaluation`, `handover_export`); structured state reuses
`knowledge_base` / `metric_baselines` (#44/#68/#70/#71/#72). Any batch that
genuinely needs a new table must justify it.

**Sequencing.** Batch 19 (strength watching-brief) is the self-contained, no-LLM
opener and preserves the #49 recovery-isolation invariant. Batch 20 establishes
the v3 review boundary that Batches 21 and 23 reuse. Batch 22 *extends* the Batch
17 experiment tracker (#72) rather than replacing it. Batch 23 (handover export) is
the integrative capstone (#13) and lands last because it summarizes the output of
every batch before it.

**Seasonal / year-on-year degrades gracefully.** True year-on-year needs ≥1 year
of history; the 84-night backfill seeds from ~24 Mar 2026, so real YoY comparisons
mature ~Mar 2027. Batch 21's engine ships now and reports insufficient history
until the window fills, consistent with #71's sample-size gates.

| Batch | Tier | Status | Phases | Goal | Acceptance criteria |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| ~~Batch 19 — Strength watching-brief~~ | 🟢 Mid | Shipped | 19.1 Classify strength / non-cycling sessions from already-synced Garmin activities (reuse the Batch 8 wrist-HR strength detection), with no new ingestion.<br>19.2 Compute deterministic strength rollups — frequency, volume/duration, and a load proxy — over rolling windows, reusing the `metric_baselines`/`analyses` homes rather than a new table where possible.<br>19.3 Surface an advisory strength "watching brief" (recent sessions, frequency-vs-target, trend) read-only in the daily loop / a panel and via API.<br>19.4 Preserve and test the recovery-isolation invariant: wrist-HR strength stays excluded from recovery/verdict decisions (#49). | Give Mark a light-touch advisory view of his strength work — is he doing it, is it trending, is it being neglected — without ever letting wrist-HR strength corrupt cycling recovery decisions. | Strength sessions are identified from already-synced activities with no new ingestion; deterministic frequency/volume/load-proxy rollups are reproducible over rolling windows and reuse `analyses`/`metric_baselines` rather than adding a table where possible (any new table is justified and migrated); the watching brief is advisory and read-only and never alters the Green/Amber/Red verdict or recovery protocol; the #49 exclusion of wrist-HR strength from recovery decisions is preserved and explicitly tested; backend pytest/ruff/mypy and any touched frontend surfaces build/test/lint pass. |
| ~~Batch 20 — Weekly & monthly deep reviews~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 20.1 Deterministic weekly rollup packet assembler aggregating the trailing week's sleep, recovery/HRV/readiness, training load + adherence, morning verdicts, thermal/environment, the strength brief (Batch 19), and Batch 17 insights.<br>20.2 Claude review boundary reusing the #47 pattern (thin Anthropic Messages call; store `prompt_version`/`model_name`/raw response + markdown in `analyses`, `analysis_type='weekly_review'`); narrative covers trends, wins, concerns, and concrete recommendations.<br>20.3 Monthly review variant over the wider window (`analysis_type='monthly_review'`), sharing the rollup + boundary machinery.<br>20.4 Read-only Reviews PWA surface + `GET/POST /api/v1/reviews/*`, human/API-triggered `/run`, `GET` previews never write (#71). | Turn the accumulated daily history into a periodic narrative deep-dive — a weekly and monthly review that reads trends, calls out wins and concerns, and recommends adjustments — the way a coach reviews a training block. | The weekly/monthly rollup packets are deterministic and reproducible from stored data; the review is generated through the thin Anthropic boundary with stored prompt/version metadata in `analyses` (#47) and is fakeable in tests without `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`; reviews are human/API-triggered via `POST /…/run`, idempotent per period, and `GET` previews never write (#71); the narrative respects the data-quality rules (no L/R balance, SpO2/HRV reliability window, wrist-HR strength excluded from recovery, ignore the broken Duration column); no new migration unless justified; tests cover packet assembly, the review boundary, idempotency, and the API/UI surface; backend pytest/ruff/mypy and frontend test/build/lint pass. |
| ~~Batch 21 — Year-on-year & seasonal trends~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 21.1 Deterministic seasonal/period aggregation engine that buckets history into comparable windows (month/season) with summary stats, reusing the `metric_baselines` provenance pattern (#44) and the reliability cutoffs (#45).<br>21.2 Year-on-year comparison: same-period-vs-prior-year deltas for sleep, recovery, FTP/VO2, and thermal, with explicit insufficient-history handling when <1 year exists.<br>21.3 Read-only surface via `GET /api/v1/trends/*` (and/or folded into the Reviews surface), with the evidence window/sample counts shown.<br>21.4 Optional narrative summary through the Batch 20 review boundary when enough history exists; otherwise report "insufficient history" deterministically. | Add the long-horizon lens — this period vs the same period last year, plus seasonal patterns (winter vs summer sleep, FTP seasonality, thermal) — so the coach reasons across seasons, not just the current block. | The aggregation engine produces reproducible per-window summary stats honouring the documented reliability cutoffs (#45); year-on-year comparisons compute same-period deltas and degrade gracefully — reporting insufficient history rather than misleading numbers — until a full year of data exists (history starts ~24 Mar 2026, so true YoY ~Mar 2027); the evidence window/sample counts are surfaced (consistent with #71); the read-only API/UI exposes trends without writing on `GET`; any narrative reuses the Batch 20 boundary; tests cover the windowing, the YoY deltas, and the insufficient-history paths; backend pytest/ruff/mypy and touched frontend pass. |
| ~~Batch 22 — Hypothesis evaluation~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 22.1 Per-experiment evidence-window evaluator: for each active experiment in the Batch 17 tracker (#72), gather the relevant data window and compute a deterministic before/after or correlation read using the Batch 17 insights math (slope/Pearson).<br>22.2 Conclusion recommendation mapping the evaluation to supported/refuted/inconclusive with the evidence surfaced — recommendation only, never an auto-conclude (the tracker's `concluded` stays human-gated and terminal — #72).<br>22.3 Surface the evaluation on the experiments PWA + `GET /api/v1/experiments/{id}/evaluate`; accepting a recommendation flows through the existing `POST /api/v1/experiments/*` conclude path.<br>22.4 Audit each evaluation in `analyses` (`analysis_type='experiment_evaluation'`), idempotent per subject window. | Close the loop on Mark's standing hypotheses (collagen, recovery-week disruption, 04:00 waking): automatically evaluate each experiment's evidence and recommend a conclusion for him to accept, instead of leaving the tracker a manual lifecycle. | Each active experiment gets a deterministic evidence-window evaluation reusing the Batch 17 insights math, skipping with an explicit reason when history is insufficient (#71 sample gates); the recommended outcome is one of supported/refuted/inconclusive with its evidence surfaced; the recommendation never changes experiment status on its own — concluding remains the human-gated, terminal `POST /…/conclude` action (#72); evaluations audit to `analyses` idempotently; no new migration (reuses `experiments`/`analyses`); tests cover the evaluator, the recommendation mapping, the never-auto-conclude guard, and the audit; backend pytest/ruff/mypy and frontend pass. |
| ~~Batch 23 — Auto-generated handover-doc export~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 23.1 Deterministic handover assembler gathering the full living state — KB (profile, data-quality rules, age-adjustment, sleep protocol, hypotheses), current plan/block, baselines, recent reviews (Batch 20), seasonal/YoY (Batch 21), experiments + evaluations (Batch 22), and the strength brief (Batch 19) — into a structured handover packet.<br>23.2 Generate the handover document through the Batch 20 review boundary (#47) into the doc shape Mark used to hand-write, stored in `analyses` (`analysis_type='handover_export'`) with prompt/version metadata.<br>23.3 Export to portable markdown and/or PDF, downloadable from the PWA + `GET/POST /api/v1/handover/*` (human/API-triggered).<br>23.4 Round-trip sanity: the export faithfully reflects current retained state (KB/plan/hypotheses) so it can seed another AI without Mark re-writing context. | Fulfil the product thesis (#13): the app generates the "handover doc" Mark used to hand-write to brief an AI — pulling all retained state and recent insight into one portable export — so he never writes one by hand again. | The handover assembler deterministically gathers KB + plan + baselines + recent reviews + seasonal + experiments/evaluations + strength brief into an inspectable packet; the document is generated through the thin Anthropic boundary with stored prompt/version metadata (#47), fakeable in tests without `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`; export produces portable markdown and/or PDF downloadable from the PWA, human/API-triggered with `GET` previews non-writing; the export faithfully reflects current retained state (data-quality rules and reliability cutoffs intact); no new migration unless justified; tests cover packet assembly, the generation boundary, and the export format; backend pytest/ruff/mypy and frontend test/build/lint pass. |

## Post-roadmap — daily-flow redesign batch plan

Batch ledger for the daily-flow Home redesign — re-sequencing the PWA around
Mark's actual day (wake → sleep snapshot → verdict → sleep-adjusted workout →
approve/override → Zwift → post-ride analysis → tomorrow + sleep prep) and
closing the bedroom climate loop. Same conventions as v1–v3: a batch is shipped
only after `/closeout` finishes; leave the row unstruck and `Planned` until
started. Decision numbers are assigned at `/batch-start` (next free is #99).
Builds on the world-class UI/UX redesign (PR #35, DECISIONS #90) and the
executable-coaching rail (Batches 12–13).

**Batch 28 (age-comparison axis + merged last-night table) was added to this
ledger retrospectively.** It was built ad-hoc in a 2026-06-28 session rather than
via `/batch-start`, and is recorded here for parity. It is built on
`feat/age-comparison` and **not yet shipped** — strike the row and set `Shipped`
at `/phase-closeout`. Decision: #98.

**Front-end-led, thin backend delta.** The morning verdict already rewrites the
real %FTP targets on an Amber/Red day (`services/executable_coaching.py` —
`adjust_ir_for_verdict`, Decision #30), and the morning check-in already feeds
the verdict (`services/morning_analysis.py` folds `manualEntries` into the
context packet). So most of the daily flow is *already built* — Batch 24 is a
pure presentation re-architecture over the existing `/api/v1/daily-loop` payload
with no backend change and no migration. The net-new logic is concentrated in
Batch 25 (same-day delivery + manual override) and Batch 26 (post-ride check-in
into the analysis).

**Sequencing.** Batch 24 ships first as the visible win and is independent of every
open question. Batch 25 carries the one real unknown — same-day intervals.icu →
Zwift latency — in a throwaway 25.0 spike, and supersedes the lead-days=2
auto-push (#31). Batch 26 mirrors the morning check-in after the ride. Batch 27
(fan) is a separate integration track, reusing the Garmin/Hive cloud-client pattern (no home hub), and gates
nothing before it. Tiers per #19: 24 is Mid (well-specified component work);
25–27 are High (delivery edge cases, analysis-engine wiring, a new integration +
control loop).

**Same-day supersedes #31.** Decision #31 auto-pushes approved workouts a couple of
days ahead; the product now wants the morning's sleep-adjusted session approved
and delivered *that day* ("most like having an actual coach"). Batch 25 records a
new decision superseding #31. The implementation shipped in PR #38 with same-day
push + manual override; the remaining live-use note is to observe real Zwift
appearance timing on the first same-day send.

**Batch 29 (Today-card actions + push-on-plan-set delivery) shipped in PR #44
on 2026-06-29.** Designed with Craig on 2026-06-29 (DECISIONS #99; full spec
`docs/designs/today-card-actions.md`). It
turns the Home "Today" card into the one place Mark acts on his day — showing the
next workout of *any* type with Edit/Swap/Skip (no coach changes) or
Approve/Ignore/Edit/Swap/Skip (sleep-adjusted) — and moves delivery to
**push-when-the-plan-is-set** so mornings are review-only and every action
re-syncs an already-delivered Zwift event. This **supersedes #91's
same-day-on-approval** (and #31's lead-days=2), and deliberately reverses
#29/#30's "nothing delivered without approval" for the *baseline* (approval now
gates only the morning adjustment).

**Batch 30 (Home day controls + rearrangeable week plan) shipped in PR #45 on
2026-06-30.** It turns the live plan into
day categories (cycle / weights / flexibility / rest / mixed), gives Home
day-level add/skip/actual controls while keeping each workout on the Batch 29
Today card, and replaces the old Plan page with a real grouped schedule that can
add workouts, move workouts, skip days, and swap an existing workout into a rest
day. Decision: #100. Full spec:
`docs/designs/home-day-controls-week-plan.md`.

**Batch 31 (Overnight temperature × fan × sleep chart) is specced, not started.**
Designed with Craig on 2026-06-30 from the "morning check-in should graph overnight
room temp vs when the fan was on/off/what setting" idea. It makes the Batch 27 fan
autopilot **legible**: the room temperature is already captured every 15 min
(`temperature_readings`), but the fan's on/off/speed history is only *logged*, never
persisted — so the batch adds a `fan_state_readings` time-series table written by
`run_fan_control`, a pure read-only `GET /api/v1/bedroom/overnight` join (temp + fan +
the night's sleep), a recharts dual-axis chart on `/bedroom`, and a one-line glance on
Home. A 2026-06-30 prod read confirmed the room runs warm enough that the fan fires
every night now, so there is real variation to plot. Decision number assigned at
`/batch-start` (next free #101). Full spec: `docs/designs/bedroom-overnight-chart.md`.

**Batch 32 (Plan page tap-to-move day picker) shipped (PR #48, squash `5d7804f`), prod-verified.** Designed
with Craig on 2026-07-01 from a "drag-and-drop between days?" idea for the weekly
plan page. The decision was **not** to use drag-and-drop: the Plan page
(`/delivery`) is edited by Mark on his phone, and touch-dragging a card across a
vertically scrolling day list is unreliable for the primary user. Instead it
replaces the page's two fragmented move controls — the per-workout `Move <date>`
trio (limited to the next 3 days) and the separate rest-day swap-in list — with
**one bottom-sheet day picker** per workout that can move a session to any day in
either direction. The picker is built as a reusable `MoveWorkoutSheet` (so Home's
Today-card swap can adopt it later) over the page's plan window, widened 7→14 days
so "push it into next week" works without a separate calendar. It is
**frontend-only**: both existing controls already call the same
`ExecutableCoachingService.swap_day` (move when the target is empty, swap when
occupied, either direction — #99/#97), so there is no backend change and no
migration. Shipped verification on the merge SHA `5d7804f`: Railway and Vercel
same-origin `/api/v1/health` both returned that SHA, web `/` returned `200`, and
unauthenticated `POST /api/v1/workout-delivery/planned-workouts/{id}/swap`
returned `401` both direct and through the Vercel rewrite. Decision #103. Full spec:
`docs/designs/plan-move-day-picker.md`.

**Batch 33 (Bedroom overnight temperature verdict) is specced, not started.**
Designed with Craig on 2026-07-01 as a direct, small follow-on to Batch 31: rather
than making Mark read the overnight chart, classify each night's room into the
app's existing Green/Amber/Red vocabulary from minutes spent at/above the
19.5 °C / 20.0 °C thresholds Batch 31 already charts, shown as a badge next to
the Home glance and the `/bedroom` chart header. Purely additive over
`services/bedroom_overnight.py`'s existing `summarize_overnight` — no new table,
no new endpoint, no migration. Decision number assigned at `/batch-start` (next
free #104). Full spec: `docs/designs/bedroom-temperature-verdict.md`.

**Batch 34 (Bedroom temperature × sleep correlation) is specced, longer-term, not
started.** Discussed with Craig on 2026-07-01 as the "does the room actually cost
sleep, and could that inform the fan's own thresholds" idea. It deliberately
reuses the existing Batch 17 driver-correlation engine
(`insights.compute_drivers`/`DRIVER_KEYS`) and the Batch 22 `early_waking_0400`
experiment evaluator rather than building new statistics — it just gives them new
candidate driver values (bedroom warning/critical minutes, fan-run minutes) from
the Batch 31 series, closing an item Batch 31 explicitly deferred (DECISIONS #101
non-goals). Advisory-only by design (#71/#72): it never writes to
`fan_control.py`'s thresholds itself, and needs weeks of accumulated
`fan_state_readings` before it has anything to say, so it is sequenced well after
Batch 31/33 have been live, not immediately following them. Decision number
assigned at `/batch-start` (next free #105). Full spec:
`docs/designs/bedroom-temperature-sleep-correlation.md`.

**Batches 35–37 (Home refinements) are specced, not started.** Reviewed with
Craig on 2026-07-01 from four Home-page thoughts, decomposed into three batches
that reinforce each other (each shrinks the surface the next one organises), to be
built in order 35 → 36 → 37. They are refinements on the Batch 24 single-phase
Home and the Batch 28 merged last-night table, all frontend-only except where
noted. Decision numbers assigned at `/batch-start` (next free #106).

**Batch 35 (Last night as the single morning hub)** combines two of the ideas
that both restructure the one "Last night's sleep" card, so they ship as one
coherent card change: (1) fold the baseline **range** into the Home
`MetricComparisonTable` and tint last night's number by whether it sat in range —
which makes the standalone `/baselines` page redundant, so it is **retired** (the
range data — `lowerQuartile`/`upperQuartile` — is already on the daily-loop
payload, and `/baselines` is only reachable from the sleep card, not any tab); and
(2) pull the **retrospective** overnight-room read (`OvernightGlance` + the Batch
33 room verdict) into that same card, leaving **tonight's live** fan/bedroom
controls in the evening card. Partially reverses Batch 28's "keep the `/baselines`
link" (#98). 🟢 Mid, frontend-only, no migration. Full spec:
`docs/designs/last-night-morning-hub.md`.

**Batch 36 (Unified Today card)** collapses Home's "today's workout" from a
summary card **plus** N separate per-session cards into **one** Today card — day
header (with the verdict badge shown **once**, not duplicated per session),
session rows each keeping their own Edit/Swap/Skip/Approve controls scoped, and a
day-level footer (Add / Skip day / "I did something else"). Pure recomposition of
existing pieces (`DayPlanCard` + `TodayCard`); Batch 29's delivery-action contract
and the `/api/v1/daily-loop` payload are unchanged. 🟢 Mid, frontend-only, no
migration. Full spec: `docs/designs/unified-today-card.md`.

**Batch 37 (Collapse-not-remove Home sections)** changes Home from **swapping**
whole section-sets by phase (Batch 24, where off-phase sections are *absent* — a
ride makes the sleep snapshot disappear) to **keeping every section present but
collapsing** the ones that aren't primary for the current state, so nothing ever
disappears from Home and object permanence is preserved. Keeps **data state** (not
the clock) as the driver of *what's primary* — the clock only nudges *ordering*
(float bedroom-prep up in the evening), never adds or hides a section. Sequenced
**after** 35 + 36 because those shrink Home to a few rich cards first, so the
collapse model reads as a short list of panels, not a wall of drawers. Supersedes
the Batch 24 remove-model (referenced as the "read-first Home" in #91/#97). 🔴
High (revises a shipped Home model + needs the expand/order judgment), frontend-
only, no migration. Full spec: `docs/designs/home-collapse-not-remove.md`.

**Batches 38–39 (in-app guided non-cycling sessions) are WITHDRAWN (2026-07-02,
DECISIONS #108).** They were specced with Craig on 2026-07-01 from the idea that
non-cycling workouts should be *coached through in the app* the way a bike workout
is coached through in Zwift — an in-app interval **player** for strength (38) and an
uploaded follow-along **video** for flexibility (39), each logging completion into a
new `guided_sessions` table and reconciling it with the Garmin activity. **Dropped
because Mark tracks his strength and flexibility sessions on his watch and only
wants the *post-workout analysis* in the app, not an in-app player to run the
session** — so the players, the `guided_sessions` table + migration, and the
completion/reconciliation machinery are all unneeded. The specs
`docs/designs/strength-guided-player.md` and `docs/designs/flexibility-video-player.md`
are kept but banner-marked WITHDRAWN (history, not deletion). This surfaced a gap —
Mark wanted the analysis for **both** strength and flexibility, but only flexibility
had a per-session read planned (Batch 40); strength had only the Batch 19 rollup
brief. That gap is filled by the new **Batch 43 (post-strength analysis)** below.
The reserved decision numbers #109 (Batch 38) and #110 (Batch 39) are retired unused.

**Batches 40–43 (non-cycling activity analysis) are specced, not started.** Batches
40–42 were specced with Craig on 2026-07-02 after a live census of Mark's **full**
Garmin history (4,280 activities, Dec 2014 → Jul 2026, 10 `activityType.typeKey`s)
surfaced three near-daily non-cycling habits the coach is blind to — **mobility,
walking, and breathwork**; **Batch 43 (post-strength analysis)** was added the same
day in the 38/39 replan (DECISIONS #108) as strength's per-session counterpart to
Batch 40. Four batches, buildable roughly in order 40 → 41 → 42 with 43 alongside 40
(independent of each other and of the Home-refinement batches 35–37; Batch 40 is the
flagship, 43 its closest sibling). Each maps a non-cycling type onto the *right*
existing pattern — the Batch 8 per-session analysis, the Batch 19 deterministic
brief, or the morning-verdict lever — rather than forcing all through the
power-centric ride analysis. Decision numbers assigned at `/batch-start` (40 → #110,
41 → #111, 42 → #112, 43 → #113, after #108 the replan and Batch 37's #109).
**Landmine carried into every spec:** Garmin's `other` bucket is two populations — 47 recent
"…Mobility Workout" sessions (`distance 0`) **and** 153 old 2016–2020 misclassified
road rides (`distance > 0`, already matched as rides by name) — so the flexibility
selector keys on the activity **name**, never `typeKey == "other"`.

**Batch 40 (Post-flexibility/mobility analysis)** gives the near-daily mobility
routine the per-session read cycling gets: the *same* Batch 8 architecture (hourly
poll → packet → Anthropic boundary → `analyses` `analysis_type='post_flexibility'`
→ daily-loop) but a **lean, purpose-built packet** (duration, HR-vs-resting,
consistency/streak, planned session, check-in) and a mobility-coach prompt, because
a 15-min stretch has no power/cadence/FTP/stamina/time-series. Name-based selector
(yoga excluded); the ~47 existing sessions are backfilled. 🔴 High (analysis-engine
prompt + new packet), backend + frontend, no migration. Full spec:
`docs/designs/post-flexibility-analysis.md`.

**Batch 41 (Walking integration)** treats 450 walks as the Z1–Z2 aerobic base /
active recovery they are, with (1) a deterministic **walking brief** (Batch 19
clone), (2) additive **active-recovery volume context** in the morning packet
(verdict math untouched), and (3) a **threshold-gated per-session analysis** for
*deliberate* walks (≥ ~30 min or ~3 km) on an **HR/pace** packet (not power),
`analysis_type='post_walk'`. Ambient walks stay brief-only; walking already carries
per-second detail (#93), so no new ingestion. 🔴 High, backend + frontend, no
migration. Full spec: `docs/designs/walking-integration.md`.

**Batch 42 (Breathwork integration)** tracks the near-daily breathwork habit with a
deterministic **consistency brief** (Batch 19 clone) and — the actionable part — a
**verdict recovery-lever**: on a Red/low-readiness/unbalanced-HRV morning the
verdict *recommends* a breathwork session via an additive `plan_adjustments` string,
using the recovery signal it already computes. No per-session analysis (a 3-min
drill has nothing to analyse) and no change to the Green/Amber/Red classification.
🔴 High (touches verdict output), backend + frontend, no migration. Full spec:
`docs/designs/breathwork-integration.md`.

**Batch 43 (Post-strength analysis)** is strength's per-session read — the direct
counterpart to Batch 40 for the sessions Mark tracks on his watch — added in the
2026-07-02 replan (DECISIONS #108) after the in-app strength *player* (old Batch 38)
was withdrawn. Same Batch 8 machinery as Batch 40 (hourly poll →
`generate_for_pending_strength` → lean packet → thin Anthropic boundary → `analyses`
`analysis_type='post_strength'` → daily-loop), keyed on the **Garmin strength
activity**. It is even higher-reuse than Batch 40: the selector already exists
(`is_strength_activity` via `exclude_from_recovery`, #49/#80) and the consistency
read reuses Batch 19's `compute_strength_rollup`, so the only new pieces are a lean
HR/consistency packet (no power/FTP/time-series) and a strength-coach prompt. It
*complements* the Batch 19 rollup brief (that is the weekly watching-brief; this is
the per-session narrative). Recovery isolation (#49/#80) preserved — strength stays
advisory. 🔴 High (analysis-engine prompt + new packet), backend + frontend, no
migration. Full spec: `docs/designs/post-strength-analysis.md`.

**Batch 44 (Interval-resolved ride analysis)** specced with Craig on 2026-07-02 after
Mark reviewed the app's post-ride read against Copilot's and named a real accuracy bug:
it *"bases it on average power expecting the power for the full workout to be in sweet
spot range, which isn't right — only the sweet spot intervals will be… it needs to
analyse the workout as a set, not base it all on its name."* A code audit confirmed it:
the `post_workout` packet hands Claude the **whole-ride** `avgPowerWatts` + a whole-ride
`timeSeriesSummary.power.avg` + a coarse zone histogram and the **planned** workout, but
never the **executed effort segmented into intervals and graded against each interval's
target** — so on any structured session the blended average sits below the work band
(warm-up + recovery + cool-down drag it down) and the model either anchors on it or
pattern-matches the **name**. This is the **first batch that goes back *into* the cycling
packet** to enrich it (Batches 40–43 forked *lean* packets away from it *because* those
non-cycling types have no power/time-series); cycling is the one type that carries
per-second power, and today we flatten it. The fix reuses the two things already shipped —
Batch 12.1's `build_structured_workout_ir` (ordered steps with `durationSec` +
`powerStartPct`/`EndPct` %FTP targets) and the DECISIONS #93 per-second `ActivityTimeSeries`
— to segment the trace on the IR's interval boundaries and grade each **work** interval on
its own target (warm-up/recovery/cool-down power described, never graded), with a `fade`
flag that grounds "no fade / no surges". No new Garmin call and **no migration** in v1;
Garmin ground-truth splits (`get_activity_splits`, which would also unlock free/outdoor
rides) and a concision/density pass (Mark's deflected "refined vs dense" question) are
deliberately deferred. The recovery decision and Green/Amber/Red are untouched — narrative
+ grading only. 🔴 High (analysis-engine prompt + packet). Full spec:
`docs/designs/interval-resolved-ride-analysis.md`.

| Batch | Tier | Status | Phases | Goal | Acceptance criteria |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| ~~Batch 24 — Time-aware home (daily-flow rebuild)~~ | 🟢 Mid | Shipped | 24.1 Add a `useDailyPhase` hook deriving the day phase from **data state, not the clock** — pre-ride = today's `morningAnalysis` present with no post-workout analysis yet; post-ride = a post-workout analysis exists for today — with time only as a tiebreaker, so it is correct whether Mark rides at 06:00 or 18:00.<br>24.2 Rebuild `pages/DashboardPage.tsx` into the single-phase flow: verdict hero → compact sleep snapshot → today's workout card (this phase only); post-ride swaps to ride analysis + tomorrow + sleep-prep + bedroom. Strength/rest days render a clean "nothing to ride today" state.<br>24.3 Demote the dense reads to tap-to-expand: the metrics-vs-baselines table, the full morning markdown read, and bedroom/weather detail move off Home into lightweight detail routes reachable from each card's chevron; nothing is hard-hidden (bottom-nav tabs + chevrons keep every read reachable).<br>24.4 Tests: phase derivation across fixtures, each Home state (pre-ride / post-ride / rest-day / offline), and the detail routes; rewrite `DashboardPage.test.tsx`. | Replace the read-everything dashboard with a calm, time-aware Home that surfaces the one step of Mark's day that matters now and keeps the rich data one tap away — using only the existing `/api/v1/daily-loop` payload. | Home renders exactly one coherent phase at a time, chosen from data state (verified across pre-ride, post-ride, rest-day, and offline fixtures); the demoted reads (metrics-vs-baselines table, full morning read, bedroom/weather detail) no longer sit on Home but remain reachable via card chevrons and the existing tabs (no hard-hide); no backend change, no new endpoint, no migration; frontend test/build/lint pass and the backend suite is untouched. |
| ~~Batch 25 — Same-day delivery + manual override~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 25.0 De-risk (throwaway spike, outside the repo like `~/garmin-spike`): time intervals.icu → Zwift same-day delivery end to end, and decide the trigger — live push on morning approval vs. pre-stage the base session overnight and push only the adjustment at wake. Spec kept, banner-marked WITHDRAWN: `docs/designs/strength-guided-player.md`. | — | — |

## Post-roadmap — passive-first loop batch plan

Batch ledger for the **passive-first reassessment** (2026-07-03) — re-reading the
app against Mark's refined user story: two nested feedback loops (**last night's
sleep → today's training**, daily; and a **completed multi-week block → the next
block**, per block), run on the principle **"effortless, not empty"** — the app
does the work and reaches out, while the rich data stays there for Mark to browse
(he enjoys it). Same conventions as v1–v3: a batch is shipped only after
`/closeout` finishes; leave the row unstruck and `Planned` until started. Decision
numbers assigned at `/batch-start` (next free is **#117**).

**What already exists (the reassessment's finding).** Most of the loop is built:
the wake-triggered morning verdict (sleep → readiness → sleep-adjusted plan via
`executable_coaching`), per-session post-workout reads for all five modalities
(ride / strength / flexibility / walk + the breathwork brief), and — crucially —
the real-world actuation Mark wants: the **Batch 27 Dreo fan autopilot already
drives the bedroom temperature overnight**. The corrected "effortless, not empty"
principle is also already well served by the Home (collapse-not-remove) + Trends /
Reviews / bedroom chart / interval-execution split. The structure is sound; these
batches are **connective tweaks, not a rebuild.**

**The gaps these batches close.** (1) The two highest-value outputs — the morning
verdict and each post-workout analysis — are generated silently and **never
pushed**; only the static 20:00 nudge + thermal/stale alerts push, so the app is
browse-first when the story wants push-first. (2) The evening thermal nudges still
tell Mark to hand-cool the room as if the fan autopilot doesn't exist. (3) There
is **no projection of how today's training will affect tonight's sleep** (the
"Tonight" section is the static protocol). (4) **Block-to-block progression
doesn't exist** — `generate_block_plan` is profile/FTP-only and never reads how
the last block went. (5) The loop is **implicit** — `DailyPhase` is `pre_ride |
post_ride | rest_day` (ride-shaped, no evening phase), which is why the pushes are
piecemeal.

**Sequencing.** **Batch 45** (proactive push + fan-reconciled nudges) ships first
— smallest, highest-impact, turns the app push-first and fixes the fan/nudge
contradiction. **Batch 46** (evening sleep projection) and **Batch 47**
(block-to-block progression) build the two missing loop stages and can proceed in
parallel — 46 closes the daily loop back to sleep, 47 builds the second, per-block
coupling. **Batch 48** (explicit loop model) is the **optional consolidating
refactor** that makes the loop first-class — deferrable, sequenced last, worth
doing only once the piecemeal wiring of 45–47 costs more than the refactor. Tiers
per #19: all 🔴 High (scheduler edge cases, analysis-engine reasoning, verdict /
plan logic, a shipped-model revision).

**Batch 45 (Proactive push + fan-reconciled nudges)** turns the app push-first.
The morning verdict and each post-workout analysis are generated by the scheduler
but **never pushed** — only the static 20:00 nudge + thermal/stale alerts reach
Mark — so today he must open the app to find his verdict/read. This wires a push
into the two existing completion points (`run_morning_weather_sync` after
`generate_and_store`; the hourly poll after `generate_for_pending_*`), reusing
`send_notification` + the `_send_once` `analyses`-tag idempotency so each
verdict/analysis pushes **exactly once** (09:30-backstop + regeneration safe). It
also reconciles the evening thermal nudges with the Batch 27 fan autopilot: defer
the manual pre-cool/seal nudges when `fan_auto_enabled` and the loop is
applying/holding, and escalate a "check the fan" push **only** when the fan can't
cope (`unreachable` / `no_data` / can't-reach-target) — the "notify only if he must
physically act" model. No migration. 🔴 High. Full spec:
`docs/designs/proactive-push-fan-reconciled.md`.

**Batch 46 (Evening sleep projection)** closes the daily loop **back to sleep**.
Today the forward-looking read is training-only ("impact on tomorrow") and the
"Tonight" Home section is the static protocol; nothing projects how today's
training will affect tonight's sleep. A deterministic, advisory `sleep_projection`
derives a qualitative directional read (**no numeric score** — false precision, per
#114) from today's training load + Mark's own measured sleep drivers (Batch 17/34)
+ the overnight weather, and layers 1–2 personalised prep actions onto the static
KB protocol, surfaced in the Tonight section (and optionally pushed via Batch 45).
Advisory only — never touches the verdict or the fan thresholds (#71/#72); degrades
to the plain protocol on a rest day / before driver history exists. 🔴 High. Full
spec: `docs/designs/evening-sleep-projection.md`.

**Batch 47 (Block-to-block progression)** builds the second feedback coupling Mark
named — **completed multi-week block → next block**. `generate_block_plan` is
profile/FTP-only and never reads how the last block went, though the signals are
all shipped (Batch 17 FTP-drift, Batch 20 rollups, Batch 44 execution grades,
`manual_entries` adherence). A deterministic `block_progression` core aggregates
the completed block's load / adherence / execution / drift / trend into a
next-block proposal (recommended FTP + focus carry-forward) that **seeds** the
generator draft with its evidence — the athlete still refines-then-locks
(#16/#69), nothing auto-applies. Reuses the existing engines, no new stats, no
LLM, no migration. 🔴 High. Full spec:
`docs/designs/block-to-block-progression.md`.

**Batch 48 (Explicit daily/block loop model) — optional, consolidating.** The loop
is implicit across scheduler jobs, Home sections, and services, which is why the
pushes are hand-wired and why `DailyPhase` is ride-shaped (`pre_ride | post_ride |
rest_day`, `post_ride` off ride analyses only, no evening phase). This
behaviour-preserving refactor makes the day/block loop a first-class state model
with an orchestration seam ("where is Mark + what's next") that Batches 45–47 hook
into, generalises the phase to any modality (a strength/walk-only day advances to
post-training), and gives evening a real `wind_down` phase instead of a 20:00 clock
nudge. **Deferrable** — 45–47 ship without it; sequenced last, when the piecemeal
wiring costs more than the refactor. No new coaching logic, no migration. 🔴 High.
Full spec: `docs/designs/explicit-loop-model.md`.

| Batch | Tier | Status | Phases | Goal | Acceptance criteria |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| ~~Batch 45 — Proactive push + fan-reconciled nudges~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 45.1 Push the **morning verdict** on generation — in `run_morning_weather_sync` after `analysis_result.generated`, send one verdict push (colour + one-line headline, `data.url='/'`), idempotent per (profile, subject_date) via the `_send_once` `analyses`-tag pattern so the 09:30 backstop + any regeneration never double-push.<br>45.2 Push each **post-workout analysis** on generation — after each `generate_for_pending_*` pass, send one push per **newly generated** analysis (ride / strength / flexibility / walk), idempotent per `activity_id` so a newer check-in / `PROMPT_VERSION` bump doesn't re-push; breathwork has no per-session analysis (#112) so nothing to push.<br>45.3 **Fan-reconcile** the evening/thermal nudges (`evaluate_thermal_alert` / `run_monitoring_alerts`): when `fan_auto_enabled` and the latest `fan_state_readings.action` ∈ {apply, hold, winddown} suppress the manual pre-cool/seal nudges; escalate a "check the fan" push only on {unreachable, no_data} or room-≥-critical-while-fan-maxed; keep the manual protocol nudges unchanged when the autopilot is off.<br>45.4 Quiet-hours honesty (a suppressed push still records its audit row — no retry) + dedupe/idempotency tests + green gates. | Make the app push-first — proactively deliver the morning verdict and every post-workout read the moment they land, and stop telling Mark to hand-cool a room the Batch 27 fan is already managing — so the coach reaches out instead of waiting to be opened. | The morning verdict and each ride/strength/flexibility/walk analysis send **exactly one** web-push when generated, idempotent across the 09:30 backstop and any regeneration (tagged `analyses` dedupe, reusing `_send_once` / `send_notification`), honouring quiet hours (suppressed pushes still audit, no retry); the evening thermal nudges defer to the Batch 27 autopilot when `fan_auto_enabled` and the loop is applying/holding/winding-down, and escalate a "check the fan" push only when the fan is unreachable/no-data or cannot reach target, while the existing manual protocol nudges are preserved unchanged when the autopilot is off; | ~~Batch 46 — Evening sleep projection~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 46.1 Pure DB-free `services/sleep_projection.py`: today's training-load signals (late / high-intensity / big-TSS / evening timing) + Mark's measured sleep drivers (Batch 17 `compute_drivers` + Batch 34 bedroom keys) + overnight weather → a **qualitative directional read** (no numeric sleep-score prediction, per #114) + 1–2 **personalised** prep actions layered on the static KB `sleep_protocol`; rest day / insufficient driver history → falls back to the plain protocol.<br>46.2 Surface in the **Tonight** Home section (`SleepPrepBody`) with its evidence one tap away; optionally append an "impact on tonight's sleep" line to the post-workout read.<br>46.3 *(optional, deferred)* Push the personalised evening projection via the Batch 45 rail, superseding the static 20:00 nudge on days it has something to say (idempotent per subject-date; optional `analyses` `analysis_type='sleep_projection'` audit row).<br>46.4 Tests (directional read + prep actions across hard-late/easy-early/rest and warm/cool overnight; no numeric score; static-protocol fallback) + green gates. | Close the loop back to sleep — project how today's training is likely to affect tonight's sleep and turn the static evening protocol into a personalised wind-down, so Mark can prepare the room and routine for the best chance of a good night. | Shipped in PR #66 (`5bf9940`): backend + frontend, no migration. | ~~Batch 47 — Block-to-block progression~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 47.1 Pure DB-free `services/block_progression.py`: aggregate the **completed** block's stats into a `BlockOutcome` — achieved-vs-planned load + adherence (Batch 20 rollups + `manual_entries`), execution-grade summary (Batch 44 per-interval `on`/`over`/`under`), FTP-drift verdict (Batch 17), and recovery/verdict trend — then map it to a **next-block proposal**: recommended FTP (bump on over-target + rising drift; hold/cut on under-target + falling drift), focus carry-forward, and a structural nudge (e.g. extra recovery on a degraded trend). | ~~Batch 48 — Explicit daily/block loop model *(optional, consolidating)*~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 48.1 A single day/block **loop-state model** (`services/daily_loop_state.py` + a generalised `useDailyPhase`): the day advances morning → training → post-training → evening wind-down → night; generalise `post_ride` → **`post_training`** off any `post_*` analysis (ride/strength/flexibility/walk) and add a first-class **`wind_down`** evening phase (not just the `EVENING_HOUR` clock reorder); the block advances build/recovery/…/consolidation → next block.<br>48.2 An **orchestration seam** ("where is Mark in his day/block + what's next") that Batches 45/46/47 consume instead of each re-deriving state.<br>48.3 Point `homeSections`/`useDailyPhase` at the generalised phase (non-ride days lead with their post-session read; evening is a real phase), preserving the existing per-state Home renders.<br>48.4 Tests (phase derivation across all modalities + rest + wind-down; block-phase transitions; Home primary selection; no visual regression) + green gates. | Make the loop a first-class object — model Mark's day and training block as explicit states with an orchestration seam, generalise the cycling-shaped `DailyPhase` to any modality, and give evening a real wind-down phase — so the passive-push, sleep-projection, and block-progression work hooks into one loop model instead of each re-deriving where he is. | An explicit day/block loop-state model derives the current phase from **any** modality (a strength/walk/flexibility/breathwork-only day advances to post-training, not stuck pre-ride) and adds a first-class evening wind-down phase (replacing the 20:00 clock-only reorder); an orchestration seam answers "where is Mark + what's next" that Batches 45–47 consume; Home's primary-section selection reads the generalised phase with the existing per-state renders preserved; it is a **behaviour-preserving refactor** — no change to the verdict/fan/analysis engines and no new coaching logic; **deferrable** and sequenced after 45–47; no migration; backend pytest/ruff/mypy and frontend test/build/lint pass. Shipped in PR #68 (`d9060a1`): backend + frontend, no migration, no LLM. Scope chosen at `/batch-start` was **model + frontend, no rewire** — a pure `services/daily_loop_state.py` generalises the phase (`post_ride`→`post_training` off any modality; a first-class evening `wind_down`) and classifies the block (`consolidation` = end-of-block boundary), with `describe_loop_state` as the orchestration seam; the daily-loop payload gains a read-only `loopState` and the generalised `useDailyPhase`/`homeSections` read it (a non-ride day advances to its post-session read; evening leads with Tonight) — but the shipped Batch 45–47 wiring is left untouched, so the literal "45–47 consume the seam" is intentionally scoped to available-not-rewired. Behaviour-preserving beyond those two intended generalisations; no verdict/fan/analysis-engine change, no new coaching logic, `loopState` optional in the shared schema so pre-48 cached payloads still parse. CI green across backend pytest/ruff/mypy, Alembic migration check, security audit, web build, and Vercel preview; production smoke passed on Railway + Vercel same-origin health (`sha=d9060a1`), web `/` 200, and auth-gated `GET /api/v1/daily-loop` 401 direct and via Vercel. Decision #118. Full spec: `docs/designs/explicit-loop-model.md`. |

## Post-roadmap — Home & navigation UX batch plan

Batch ledger for the **Home & navigation UX read** (2026-07-03) — a world-class
UI/UX pass over the shipped app against the two-loop intent (**sleep→training**
daily, **block→block** per block) on the **"effortless, not empty"** principle,
now that the app is **push-first** (Batch 45). Same conventions as v1–v3 and the
passive-first plan: a batch is shipped only after `/closeout` finishes; leave the
row unstruck and `Planned` until started. Decision numbers assigned at
`/batch-start` (next free is **#119**).

**The finding.** The bones are strong — three-tabs-plus-More (`navConfig.ts`),
verdict-first Home (`VerdictHero`), and collapse-not-remove (Batch 37) are all
right and are **kept**. Two structural gaps remain: (1) the layout is
training-forward — the *sleep* half of the daily loop (last night, tonight's
projection, the Batch 27 bedroom-fan autopilot) has **no nav presence**, reachable
only via Home detail-links, while `Trends` (a browse-when-curious surface) holds a
primary slot; and (2) Home hasn't caught up to push-first — the one expanded
section is chosen by *time/phase*, so an actionable item (a pending coach
adjustment, an unlogged ride check-in) can sit **collapsed and invisible** in a
non-primary section, and the collapsed summaries don't signal that they need a tap.
A third, minor issue: several "More" labels are engineer-speak for a 57-year-old
non-technical daily user.

**Sequencing.** **Batch 49** (nav & IA refactor + Sleep hub) ships first — the
load-bearing change: primary tabs become Home / Week / Sleep, a `/sleep` hub
composes the existing sleep/bedroom surfaces (`/bedroom` is absorbed), and "More"
is re-tiered + de-jargoned. **Batch 50** (action-first Home) then makes Home's
expanded section + a new "Next" strip driven by *what needs Mark* over time-of-day,
with state-signalling collapsed summaries; it deep-links evening into the Batch 49
Sleep hub. **Batch 51** (desktop two-column) is an **optional, low-priority**
layout-only polish, sequenced last. All three are **frontend-only, no migration**.
Tiers per #19: 49 🟢 Mid (component/route work), 50 🔴 High (revises the shipped
Home selection model), 51 🟢 Mid (optional).

**Batch 49 (Navigation & IA refactor + Sleep hub)** gives the sleep loop a front
door. Primary tabs become **Home / Week / Sleep**; a new `/sleep` hub with a
**Last night | Tonight** split composes existing components (`MetricComparisonTable`,
`OvernightGlance`, `BedroomOvernightChart`, `SleepPrepBody`, `BedroomBody`) — no
new data — and `/bedroom` redirects into it; `Trends` is demoted to "More", which
is re-tiered into **For you** (Reviews, Trends, Holiday) / **Coaching** (New
training block, Experiments) / **Setup** (Coach memory, Handover, Settings) with
de-jargoned labels (Plan→Week, Tests→Experiments, Plan builder→New training block,
Coach state→Coach memory; "Handover" kept — Mark's own word). `TabBar`/`MoreMenu`/
`TopBar` render off `navConfig.ts` generically, so no structural nav change. No
migration. 🟢 Mid. Full spec: `docs/designs/navigation-sleep-hub.md`.

**Batch 50 (Action-first Home)** catches Home up to push-first. A deterministic,
payload-only `nextAction` resolver drives a single "Next" strip under the verdict
hero (pending coach change > unlogged ride check-in > daily check-in >
protect-sleep > all-clear), and the same resolver **overrides** the phase→primary
selection so the section holding the top action is the one expanded — regardless of
time of day. Collapsed section summaries gain a warning tone + dot when they need a
tap; the duplicated Today verdict badge is dropped; and (given Batch 49) evening
`tonight`/`bedroom` become compact cards that deep-link into the Sleep hub. All
signals already ride `/api/v1/daily-loop`; no backend change, no migration. 🔴 High.
Full spec: `docs/designs/action-first-home.md`.

**Batch 51 (Desktop two-column dashboard) — optional.** On `md+` viewports, lay the
ordered Home section list out as two lanes (act: verdict/Next/Today/After-your-ride;
context: Last night/Tonight/Bedroom) instead of one narrow column, using the same
section components; mobile stays the single stacked column and the section/action
model is unchanged. The real user is on a phone PWA, so this is polish, not a loop
gap — **deferrable, sequenced last**. No migration. 🟢 Mid. Full spec:
`docs/designs/desktop-dashboard-layout.md`.

Decision assigned at `/batch-start`. Full spec: `docs/designs/desktop-dashboard-layout.md`. |

## Post-roadmap — Front-end premium UX batch plan

Batch ledger for the **front-end premium review** (2026-07-03) — a world-class
UI/UX pass over the shipped app. North-star agreed with Craig: **calm, premium
health companion** (quiet confidence, one clear action per screen, data on
demand); brand latitude **keep CheckMark, integrate it better**. Same conventions
as the prior plans: a batch is shipped only after `/closeout` finishes; leave the
row unstruck and `Planned` until started. Decision numbers assigned at
`/batch-start` (next free is **#122**). Overview + rationale + the annotated live
walk-through: `docs/designs/frontend-premium-review.md`.

**The finding.** The architecture is genuinely good — real token system, sound
3-tab IA, verdict-first Home, collapse-not-remove — and is **kept**. The gap is
**execution polish + brand presence**: on the live app the dark surface tiers sit
in one narrow near-black band so cards don't separate and Home reads as a flat
monotone wall (P0); form inputs are dark-on-dark and barely legible — an
accessibility problem for a 57-year-old daily user (P0); the verdict, the
product's heartbeat, is an uncrafted faint box (P0); and there is **no logomark
anywhere in the running app** even though a strong mark (a checkmark-as-heartbeat
on a teal→green tile with a verdict-gauge arc) already exists as the PWA/favicon
icon (P1). Net: it reads as competent developer-dark, not premium calm companion.

**Sequencing.** **Batch 52** (design foundations) ships first — the load-bearing
change: it rebuilds the surface/elevation ramp, the input/control tier, and the
label/type system at the token + primitive layer, so every later batch inherits a
premium base. **Batch 53** (branded verdict, hero & login) then makes the identity
felt — the existing mark brought in-app, a crafted `VerdictHero`, a mark-led login
splash, a top-bar mark, and the "Next" strip promoted to a real action band.
**Batch 54** (Home hierarchy & calm density) turns Home from a wall of equal
accordions into a curated brief (recede secondary sections, collapse the button
cluster to one primary + overflow, tighten the first screen, animate expand).
**Batch 55** (screen polish & states) applies the system across Sleep / Check-in /
Week and gives loading/empty/error states character. All four are **frontend-only,
no migration**. Tiers per #19: 52 🔴 High (system-wide visual foundation, design
judgment), 53 🔴 High (brand craft), 54 🟢 Mid (Home recomposition), 55 🟢 Mid
(applies the system).

**Batch 52 (Design foundations)** rebuilds the visual foundation. The dark
`--surface-*`/`--border*` tiers are re-spaced into a clear value ramp (the light
palette already separates well), the elevation/shadow tokens are refined, and the
input/control tier (`input`/`label`/`select`/`card`/`button` + the shared textarea
style) gets its own elevated fill, a stronger border, a clear focus ring, and
AA-legible placeholder/label. Mono-uppercase is pulled back to eyebrows / numerics
/ the wordmark; form labels become sentence-case. Token + primitive only — no
per-screen layout change, no endpoint/payload/migration. 🔴 High. Full spec:
`docs/designs/design-foundations.md`.

**Batch 53 (Branded verdict, hero & login)** weaves the identity through the app.
The existing (currently icon-only) mark is brought in-product via a `Logomark`
(login splash hero, top bar, verdict cue); `VerdictHero` is redesigned into a
crafted, elevated, branded heartbeat on the Batch 52 surfaces (Green/Amber/Red +
pending semantics unchanged); the login splash is mark-led with the wordmark
gradient actually applied; and the `NextActionStrip` becomes a full-width primary
action band tied under the verdict. Presentation only — no change to verdict logic
or `/api/v1/daily-loop`, no rename/rebrand, no migration. 🔴 High. Full spec:
`docs/designs/branded-verdict-hero-login.md`.

**Batch 54 (Home hierarchy & calm density)** turns Home into a curated brief. It
keeps collapse-not-remove (Batch 37), the action override (Batch 50), and the
desktop two-lane (Batch 51), but visually recedes the secondary/context sections
under a quiet "More detail" grouping so the eye lands on verdict → action band →
Today; the session card's five-button cluster collapses to one primary + a "More
options" overflow; the greeting folds into a compact lockup so the verdict sits
higher; summaries truncate on word boundaries; and section expand gets a subtle,
reduced-motion-aware animation. Every signal already rides `/api/v1/daily-loop`; no
payload change, no migration. 🟢 Mid. Full spec:
`docs/designs/home-hierarchy-calm-density.md`.

**Batch 55 (Screen polish & states)** finishes the pass. It applies the Batch 52
system across Check-in (legible inputs, sentence-case labels, lower density),
Sleep (surfaces, the mostly-empty "vs your age" column, the heavy evidence
disclosure), and Week (surfaces, card nesting), and adds a shared, on-brand
empty/error/offline pattern (say what happened + a clear recovery CTA) in place of
the generic "please try again" cards. Presentation only — no data/endpoint/
analysis-engine change, no migration. 🟢 Mid. Full spec:
`docs/designs/screen-polish-states.md`.
