## Post-roadmap — 2026-07-06 sleep-score age-norm batch plan

Mark's second 2026-07-06 thread (separate from the completed-workout snags in
Batch 60): the "typical" values shown next to his sleep are Garmin's young-adult
lab targets, not norms for a 57-year-old, so age-normal sleep is scored/flagged as
poor. He backed this with a Copilot "age-adjusted norms" table + sources. Verified
against the code before scoping: the app's **age-adjusted sleep score is a flat
Garmin `+4`** (`garmin_sync.py:428`, `morning_analysis.py:747`) that inherits
Garmin's per-stage young-adult penalty, and the Sleep-page **"Typical" column is a
single population *average*** that warns below the midpoint — so his complaint is
right for the score and a presentation problem for the column. Garmin's own
`sleepScores` payload (already stored in `Sleep.factors_json`) exposes the
young-adult target bands (e.g. REM optimal **21–31%**), which both proves the
point and gives us the structure to recompute against age bands. Copilot's
*direction* is right but several of its numbers aren't adoptable (REM 12–17% too
low vs Ohayon 2004; Deep 20–30% too high; Restless/Awake are device-proprietary;
some HR/HRV rows are athlete-Mark's values, not 57-yr norms). Scope chosen with
Craig: **full fix in one batch** — healthy age *bands* + a *real* age-adjusted
score (not +4). Proposed Decision **#135** (revisits #14, extends #131). Full
spec: `docs/designs/age-adjusted-sleep-norms.md`.

| Batch | Tier | Status | Phases | Goal | Acceptance criteria |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| ~~Batch 61 — Age-adjusted sleep norms & real age-adjusted score~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 61.1 `services/age_norms.py`: turn per-metric single averages into `(low, high)` **healthy age bands** (sex × decade) for the sleep-stage rows; band-aware `_classify` (in-band = neutral/good, warn only meaningfully outside, edge tolerance); demote **Restless** to descriptive-only (Garmin-proprietary, no defensible population band); general-fitness rows (VO₂max/RHR/HRV) unchanged.<br>61.2 New pure `services/sleep_scoring.py`: recompute the age-adjusted score by re-qualifying the age-sensitive components (REM/Deep/Light/Awake) against age bands using Garmin's own `factors_json.sleepScores` structure, with a **calibration guard** (all-Garmin-optimal ≈ Garmin score) and a **downgrade guard** (never below raw). Computed at analysis time from stored inputs — no migration, no re-sync; `garmin_sync.py:428`'s inline `+4` removed; `morning_analysis`/DB-history baselines/`reviews`/`chronic_patterns` call the one function when profile context exists and fall back to stored history when it does not.<br>61.3 UI: rename "Typical" → **"Healthy range (50–59)"** showing the band; add an opt-in quiet **"Garmin target"** contrast on the Sleep-page deep table (`SleepStageAgeTable.tsx`, `MetricComparisonTable.tsx`); keep the guide/not-medical footnote and Batch 55 restraint.<br>61.4 Prompt line so the LLM narrates against the age band not Garmin's qualifier; shared Zod schema picks up band low/high + Garmin target fields; bump `PROMPT_VERSION`.<br>61.5 Tests + real-night safety re-verification + gates. | Stop scoring and flagging Mark's age-normal sleep against young-adult targets: show a healthy range for his age (not a point average or Garmin's number) and make the age-adjusted score a genuine recompute instead of a flat +4. | Shipped via PR #84 / squash `7936fcb`; no migration, no new endpoint, forward-only (no historical score backfill run at closeout). ## Post-roadmap — 2026-07-07 first-open performance batch plan

Mark's report: "data is slow to load when I first open the app." Measured against
the live system before scoping so we fix the real cause. Warm production timings
(2026-07-07, unauthenticated) show the container is **not** cold-starting —
Railway `/api/v1/health` returns in ~0.10 s direct and ~0.11 s through the Vercel
proxy, because the in-process APScheduler keeps the process alive. The real causes
are two things that only line up on a fresh launch: (1) the client has **no
persisted React Query cache** and `staleTime` defaults to 0 (`apps/web/src/App.tsx`),
so a cold open blocks the whole Home screen on one round-trip behind an empty cache
and shows a full skeleton; and (2) that one blocking request — `GET
/api/v1/daily-loop` — is the fattest endpoint in the app, recomputing a **120-day**
driver correlation (`services/insights.py`) plus a chronic-pattern scan and running
~15 **sequential** DB queries on every load (`_envelope`, `get_snapshot`). Scope
chosen with Craig: **fix in one batch** — persist the cache so the last brief paints
instantly, move the deterministic correlation maths off the hot path into the daily
morning sync, thin/parallelize the snapshot round-trips, and verify Railway↔Supabase
region colocation. Proposed Decision **#136**. Full spec:
`docs/designs/first-open-performance.md`.

| Batch | Tier | Status | Phases | Goal | Acceptance criteria |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| ~~Batch 62 — First-open latency: persist cache & thin daily-loop~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 62.1 Persist the React Query cache to `localStorage` (v5 `persist-client` + `query-sync-storage-persister`): `PersistQueryClientProvider` in `App.tsx`, `staleTime`≈60 s on `useDailyLoop`, `buster`=build SHA, `maxAge` 24 h, `dehydrateOptions` persists only the daily-loop key, and login/activate/unlock/logout clear the persisted client alongside the existing `queryClient.clear()`.<br>62.2 Precompute `InsightsService.drivers()` + `ChronicPatternSuggestionService.suggestions()` once in `run_morning_weather_sync` and store via the existing `analyses` `driver_correlation` audit row (no migration); `_envelope` reads today's stored packet and falls back to live compute when missing/stale.<br>62.3 Cut & parallelize the snapshot's ~15 serial round-trips: collapse the four post-`{workout,flexibility,strength,walk}` analysis SELECTs into one `analysis_type IN (...)` query partitioned in Python, and run the three briefs (strength/walking/breathwork) concurrently via `asyncio.gather`, each on its own short-lived `AsyncSessionLocal()` (one session can't multiplex).<br>62.4 Verify Railway↔Supabase region colocation (a config-only win if mismatched) and add a `SELECT 1` warm-ping to an existing 15-min job so the first open rarely hits a cold pooled connection.<br>62.5 Before/after authenticated daily-loop timing, web persistence + backend read-through/parallel-payload tests, and gates. | Make the first open paint the last brief instantly and cut authenticated `GET /api/v1/daily-loop` server time, without changing any decision output. | Warm server confirmed (not a cold-start problem); first open with a prior cached brief renders content immediately with no full skeleton (background refetch swaps fresh data in place); authenticated daily-loop server time materially reduced against the 62.5 baseline; daily-loop payload byte-identical for a fixed DB state (verdict / #133 / #134 / #135 invariants untouched); persisted cache bounded by `maxAge` and cleared on logout; no migration; backend pytest/ruff/mypy, shared typecheck, web vitest/tsc/lint/build (Node 20) all pass; closeout prod smoke on the merge SHA. Decision #136 (assigned at `/batch-start`). Full spec: `docs/designs/first-open-performance.md`. |

## Post-roadmap — 2026-07-07 summary-feedback batch plan

Mark's 2026-07-07 ask: let him rate the accuracy of any summary the app generates —
sleep, workout, the morning verdict, or the coach's suggested workout edits — and
tell it when it's wrong. Challenged and reframed with Craig before scoping: at n=1 a
star-rating pipeline has no aggregate to learn from, so the value is the *correction*
(a one-line "I actually slept fine"), not the score, and the highest-value move is
capturing his subjective read cheaply *before* the verdict as well as correcting it
after. Mark agreed with the combination and named the real constraint — a quick
morning check-in "will be significantly less than what I'm doing now": the input must
undercut his current manual routine, not add to it ("a guide, not a magic wand").

Verified against the code before scoping: (1) every AI summary is already a single
`analyses` row (`coaching.py:413`) with a stable UUID + `analysis_type` (`morning`,
`post_workout`/`_walk`/`_strength`/`_flexibility`, `weekly_review`, `monthly_review`,
`seasonal_trend`) + `output_markdown`, so one feedback primitive keyed to
`analysis_id` covers the whole app; (2) the subjective-read→verdict loop already
exists — the manual-entry PUT fires `regenerate_after_morning_checkin`
(`daily_loop.py:1123`), so lightening the check-in is a UX job not new plumbing, and
the current `/check-in` (`CheckInPage.tsx`) is the heavy multi-card form Mark is
escaping; (3) no feedback/rating table exists; (4) the `/sleep` review is computed
client-side (`sleepReview.ts`) and is *not* an `analyses` row, so it has no server id
to attach feedback to and defers (piggybacks on the day's morning analysis).

Scope chosen with Craig: **two batches** — 63 lightens the check-in first (Mark's
felt pain), 64 adds the rate-&-correct primitive. Corrections **feed the next read**
(included in the next generation's `context_packet`, not auto-regenerated). Ratings
use **two axes by content type** — summaries: accuracy; suggested edits: agreement.
No rating dashboard/aggregation (n=1). Proposed Decision **#137** (assigned at
`/batch-start`). Full spec: `docs/designs/summary-feedback.md`.

| Batch | Tier | Status | Phases | Goal | Acceptance criteria |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| ~~Batch 63 — Lighten the morning check-in (fast path)~~ | 🟢 Mid | Shipped | 63.1 Make the `/check-in` default a **quick check-in**: a tap button-group for overall (writes `manual_entries.subjective_score`) + 2–3 one-tap chips (slept well / energy / niggle) folded into `feel`/`notes`; the BP, supplements/food, and per-workout adherence cards move behind a "More" disclosure. Reuses `manualEntryInputSchema` + `PUT /api/v1/daily-loop/{date}/manual-entry` — no new endpoint, no migration.<br>63.2 Confirm the quick save still fires `regenerate_after_morning_checkin` (`daily_loop.py:1123`, inherited via the manual-entry PUT) so the verdict + eased ride still reshape from his read.<br>63.3 Home: a one-tap quick-check-in affordance; stays optional (Batch 60 / #134) — no blocking `!manualEntry` rung reintroduced.<br>63.4 Web tests (quick-form render/save, chip→column mapping, regen still fires) + backend/shared/web gates. | Cut the daily check-in from a multi-field form to a few taps so it undercuts Mark's current manual routine ("significantly less than what I'm doing now"), without losing the check-in→verdict regeneration. | Shipped in PR #87 (squash `bc17f59`): the `/check-in` default is a 5-button "Overall" tap group (`subjectiveScore` 2/4/6/8/10) plus three one-tap chips (Slept well / Low energy → `feel`, Niggle → `notes`, toggled as a comma-joined token); BP, the free-text feel/notes inputs, supplements/food, and per-workout adherence sit behind a reused `CollapsibleSection` "More", collapsed by default and never required; no backend/shared file changed, so the existing `manualEntryInputSchema` + `PUT /manual-entry` endpoint and its `regenerate_after_morning_checkin` call are unchanged and still fire on a quick save; the check-in was already optional (Batch 60/#134) so no Home change was needed. unique `(user_id, analysis_id)` for upsert; index `(user_id, analysis_id)`.<br>64.2 `PUT /api/v1/analyses/{analysis_id}/feedback` (upsert) in the `{data, meta, errors}` envelope, **user-scoped** (404/403 if the analysis isn't the caller's); ## Post-roadmap — 2026-07-07 workout-scheduling batch plan

Mark's 2026-07-07 feedback from running the week entirely in the app: (1) he agreed
with the app that a poor-sleep day was no day for the scheduled VO2 and **juggled the
week around by hand** — his preference is to **swap sessions across the week, not
soften them** — and it "worked perfectly"; (2) the app has **Bodyweight on Monday and
Dumbbells on Saturday, the wrong way round**; (3) Saturday's ride and dumbbells are
**one combined workout**, so moving the Saturday Z2 to Thursday dragged the dumbbells
too — cycling and strength must be **separate so they move independently**.

Verified against the code before scoping: (1) points 2 and 3 share one root cause —
every build-week Saturday in `apps/api/data/plans/plan_no2.json` is a single
`bike_endurance` row titled `"Z2 + Neuromuscular + Dumbbells"` (the strength is prose
welded onto a ride, invisible to the `workout_type`-keyed day category,
`workout_categories.py:40`); (2) **multi-workout days already work end-to-end** — the
schedule returns a list per day (`plan_actions.py:33`) and the Plan page renders one
Move-able `WorkoutRow` per workout (`WeekAheadPage.tsx:208`) via the existing
version-as-slot on `(user_id, workout_date, version)` — only the importer (flat
`version=1`, `plan_import.py:201`) and swap-target detection (`_active_workout_on`
`.limit(1)`, `executable_coaching.py:898`) still assume one workout per day; (3) a
**swap-not-soften engine already exists but is unreachable** — `weekly_restructure.py`
defers hard sessions on fatigue via `GET/POST /api/v1/restructure/*` and no web page
consumes it, while the morning verdict only ever recommends softening
(`_plan_adjustments`, `morning_analysis.py:1211`).

Scope chosen with Craig: **two batches** — 65 splits the row + corrects the Mon/Sat
mapping (the visible defect Mark hit), 66 makes the coach recommend and offer a
week-swap instead of only softening (surfacing the engine that already exists).
Neither needs a migration. Proposed Decisions **#138** (65) and **#139** (66),
assigned at `/batch-start`. Full spec: `docs/designs/workout-scheduling-feedback.md`.

| Batch | Tier | Status | Phases | Goal | Acceptance criteria |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| ~~Batch 65 — Separate cycling & strength + correct Mon/Sat mapping~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 65.1 Rewrite `apps/api/data/plans/plan_no2.json`: Monday strength → the **Dumbbell** session (~22 min full-body circuit from `Dumbbell & Bodyweight 19.06.26.docx`); split each build-week Saturday into **two entries for the same `dow`** — a cycle (`bike_endurance`, "Z2 + Neuromuscular", existing bike steps minus the "Then: 20min dumbbells" tail) and a **Bodyweight** strength session — so Dumbbells↔Bodyweight swap days and Saturday's ride & strength become distinct rows.<br>65.2 `import_plan` assigns **incrementing versions per date** (cycle v1, strength v2, deterministic order) instead of a flat `version=1`, so same-day rows satisfy the `(user_id, workout_date, version)` constraint; `build_plan_rows` already emits one row per entry.<br>65.3 Scope swap-target detection (`_active_workout_on`/`swap_day`) to the **same category as the source** so moving a ride never drags a same-day strength row and swapping two ride days leaves both days' strength in place; keep the Batch 60 completed-session 409 guards.<br>65.4 Re-import to prod **forward from next Monday** (`start_date` override) so Mark's already-hand-juggled current week is preserved, then `reconcile_deliveries` re-syncs Zwift for the new bike rows — an explicit closeout step, not a blind re-run.<br>65.5 Tests (importer versioning + split-day, swap-engine category-scoped multi-workout, plan-JSON shape, web split-day render guard) + gates. | Split the welded Saturday ride+dumbbells into two independently-movable sessions and put the right strength on the right day (Dumbbells Monday, Bodyweight Saturday), so moving a ride never drags the strength with it. | Saturday shows two cards — a ride (Z2 + Neuromuscular) and a Bodyweight strength — each with its own Move; Monday shows the Dumbbell session; moving the Saturday ride to another day leaves the Saturday strength in place; swap swaps ride-for-ride and never silently drags a second same-day workout; the importer assigns per-date versions with no unique-constraint violation; the prod re-import preserves Mark's current hand-juggled week (forward-from-next-Monday) and Zwift reconciles for the new bike rows; **no migration** (existing version-as-slot); verdict / #133 / #134 / #135 invariants + delivery rules unchanged; backend pytest/ruff/mypy, shared typecheck, web vitest/tsc/lint/build (Node 20) pass; closeout prod smoke on merge SHA. Decision #138 (assigned at `/batch-start`). Full spec: `docs/designs/workout-scheduling-feedback.md`. |
| ~~Batch 66 — Swap-first recovery guidance~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 66.1 Record the preference in the knowledge base (coaching protocol): when readiness is low and a hard session (VO2/Sweet-Spot) is scheduled, **rearrange the week — move the hard session to a better day and pull an easier session forward — before softening**; closeout prod smoke on merge SHA. Decision #139 (assigned at `/batch-start`). Full spec: `docs/designs/workout-scheduling-feedback.md`. |

## Post-roadmap — 2026-07-08 workout-fidelity & feedback-loop batch plan

Mark's 2026-07-07/08 feedback after a week of accepting the app's recommendations
(five screenshots, eleven observations). Root cause verified against the code and the
plan data: **every one of the 65 bike sessions in `apps/api/data/plans/plan_no2.json`
is authored as a single collapsed step** (`{label, target: <prose>, minutes}`) with the
real structure only in a prose `summary` the delivery engine never parses — so VO2
delivers as a flat 154 W Z1 ride (the `_power_pct` `return 55` fallback,
`workout_delivery.py:782`), Z2 "65–72%" is graded "Under" against 72 (an en-dash defeats
the band regex, `:757`), warm-up/cool-down ramps never survive, and `duration_min` drifts
(VO2 60 vs ~47). Two further gaps: the post-workout read grades the **planned** VO2 row,
never the eased/substituted ride he actually did (`post_workout_analysis.py:626`); and the
"Changed it" logger sits inside the **morning** check-in, captures only minutes/RPE, and
never reaches the read. One new feature: no weekly-mix accounting exists (observation 4).

Scope: **four batches** — 67 re-authors the plan as real steps + hardens the parser (the
trunk fix, resolves 1/2/11), 68 grades the delivered ride not the stale plan (5), 69 makes
accepting a recommendation self-logging and moves logging post-ride (3), 70 adds
weekly-mix maintenance (4, decision-gated). None needs a migration; 67 is the dependency
for 68/70. Proposed Decisions **#140–#143**, assigned at `/batch-start`. Full spec:
`docs/designs/workout-fidelity-and-feedback-loop.md`.

## Post-roadmap — 2026-07-10 Mark feedback batch plan

Mark's 2026-07-10 note (one screenshot, three problems) while trying to swap the
day's scheduled "Z2 + Neuromuscular + Dumbbells" for a plain 1-hour outdoor Z2
ride. **The screenshot is the Home tab, not the Week tab** — the
`Edit / Swap day / More options` cluster and the `Duration % / Intensity % /
Apply & sync` editor only exist on `DashboardPage.tsx`. Root cause verified
against the code:

1. **Home's "+ Cycle" can't make an hour, and typing 133% throws "API error
   422".** Home's add buttons (`AddWorkoutButtons`, `DashboardPage.tsx:1021`) POST
   `{category}` only, so the backend inserts the fixed first-catalog default — a
   45-min Zone 2 endurance ride (`default_workout_for_category`,
   `plan_actions.py:208`). Home never got the editable picker the **Week tab**
   received in Batch 71 (`QuickAddSheet` + `subtype`/`durationMin`), so there is no
   add-time duration choice. To resize, the per-session Edit dial scales duration,
   but it is capped at 125% both client-side (`max={125}`,
   `DashboardPage.tsx:1317`) and server-side (`durationScalePct`
   `Field(ge=50, le=125)`, `workout_delivery.py:79`). 45×1.25 = 56 min, so an hour
   is **unreachable from the 45-min base** regardless; and an HTML `max` does not
   stop typing, so **133** is sent and Pydantic 422s. That 422 arrives as an
   array-`detail`, which `apiFetch` cannot stringify (`api.ts:88` only surfaces a
   string `detail`), so it degrades to the raw "API error 422" toast — never
   telling him the bound.
2. **No way to author a bespoke ride (some Z3, or sprints).** The cycle quick-add
   catalog is exactly endurance / sweet-spot / recovery (`QUICK_ADD_CATALOG`,
   `plan_actions.py:60`) — no tempo/Z3, no VO2/efforts, and no custom-interval
   builder anywhere. His fallback instinct is correct and already works: an
   unplanned/freeform ride is read post-hoc (the "After your ride" section,
   `postWorkoutAnalyses` with no `plannedWorkoutId`, `DashboardPage.tsx:376`) — but
   nothing in the UI tells him that is the intended path.
3. **Skip "said done" but the session is still there; there is no delete.** For a
   bike session the only destructive control is Skip (overflow "More options").
   `skip_workout` flips `status='skipped'` and deletes the Zwift event but **leaves
   `is_active=True`** (`executable_coaching.py:788` mutates only status). The
   **Week/Plan** schedule query hides skipped rows (`status != 'skipped'`,
   `plan_actions.py:233`), but the **Home** daily-loop query filters only
   `is_active` and never excludes skipped (`daily_loop.py:441`), so the skipped
   session keeps rendering on Home with no badge — indistinguishable from
   untouched. And a workout Mark *added himself* can only be skipped, never removed.

Scope: **three batches**, one per problem — 73 brings Batch 71's editable
quick-add to the Home Today card and makes the edit-dial 422 legible (resolves 1),
74 makes Home honour a skipped session and gives an added workout a real Remove
(resolves 3), 75 adds a couple of ride subtypes (tempo/Z3, a simple VO2/efforts)
and surfaces the "just ride it — I'll read it after" path for anything truly
bespoke (resolves 2). All frontend-led over endpoints that already exist; none
needs a migration. Proposed Decisions **#146–#148**, assigned at `/batch-start`.
Full spec: this section (a design doc can be added at `/batch-start` if 74's
skip-vs-remove semantics warrant one).

| Batch | Tier | Status | Phases | Goal | Acceptance criteria |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| ~~Batch 73 — Editable quick-add on the Home Today card + legible edit-dial~~ | 🟢 Mid | Shipped | 73.1 Reuse the Batch 71 `QuickAddSheet` on Home's `DayPlanBody` (`DashboardPage.tsx`) — the `+ Cycle/Weights/Flexibility` buttons open the picker (subtype + editable duration within the option's `[min,max]`) instead of instant-adding the fixed default; `addWorkoutMutation` sends `{category, subtype, durationMin}` (the endpoint + `workout_for_selection` bounds already exist from Batch 71), so a 60-min Z2 ride is one add. Home also needs the `quick-add-options` query the Week page already has.<br>73.2 Make the edit-dial error legible: clamp the Duration %/Intensity % inputs to their real bounds and show the allowed range inline; extend `apiFetch` (`api.ts:88`) to stringify FastAPI array-`detail` so a bound violation reads as a message, not "API error 422".<br>73.3 **Decide at `/batch-start`:** whether to also raise the `durationScalePct` ceiling above 125% (`workout_delivery.py:79` + `DashboardPage.tsx:1317`) or leave the dial a modest ±25% tweak now that add-time duration covers the hour case.<br>73.4 Tests (Home add opens the picker and posts subtype+duration; out-of-bounds duration surfaces the bound; edit-dial over-max shows a legible message not a raw 422) + web/backend gates. | Let Mark choose and size a ride when he adds it on Home — pick a 60-min Z2 in one step — and never see a bare "API error 422" from the resize dial. | Adding a session on the Home Today card offers the same subtype + editable-duration picker as the Week tab (Batch 71 parity), posting `subtype`/`durationMin`; a 45→60-min ride is reachable at add-time; the Edit dial rejects out-of-range input with the allowed range shown, not a raw 422, and `apiFetch` surfaces FastAPI validation detail everywhere; existing add/edit/swap/skip flows unchanged; no migration; full gates; closeout prod smoke. Decision #146 (assigned at `/batch-start`). |
| ~~Batch 74 — Home honours a skipped session + Remove for added workouts~~ | 🟢 Mid | Shipped | 74.1 Exclude skipped from Home: add `PlannedWorkout.status != WORKOUT_STATUS_SKIPPED` to the daily-loop `_planned_workouts` query (`daily_loop.py:441`) so a skipped session leaves the Today card, matching the Week `schedule()` query (`plan_actions.py:233`).<br>74.2 Give a user-added workout (`source='plan_action_add'`) a genuine **Remove** — **decided at `/batch-start`** whether Remove deactivates the row (`is_active=False`, no skipped-adherence noise) while the coach's planned sessions keep Skip's adherence-tracked semantics; Remove still deletes any pushed Zwift event.<br>74.3 UI: the added-ride row offers Remove (not just Skip buried in the overflow); a removed/skipped session disappears immediately and after reload.<br>74.4 Tests (Home excludes a skipped workout; Remove deactivates an added workout and deletes its Zwift event; planned-session Skip still records adherence; the two pages agree) + gates. | When Mark skips or removes a session it actually leaves the Home card — and a ride he added himself can be removed outright, not just skipped. | A skipped session no longer renders on Home (parity with the Week tab); an added workout has a Remove that deactivates it and clears its Zwift event; the coach's planned sessions keep Skip's adherence semantics; skip/remove persist across reload; no migration (the `status`/`is_active` columns already exist); full gates; closeout smoke. Decision #147 (assigned at `/batch-start`). |
| ~~Batch 75 — Bespoke-ish rides: more subtypes + explicit post-hoc path~~ | 🟢 Mid | Shipped | 75.1 Extend `QUICK_ADD_CATALOG` cycle options (`plan_actions.py:60`) with **tempo/threshold (Z3)** and a simple **VO2/"with efforts"** preset, authored as real structured steps (warm-up/work/recovery/cool-down at explicit %FTP) using the Batch 67 step grammar, each with sane `[min,max]` bounds.<br>75.2 Surface a plain "doing something different? just ride it — I'll read it after" affordance near the add controls / rest-day copy, pointing at the existing post-hoc read path (unplanned rides → "After your ride", `DashboardPage.tsx:376`), so Mark knows he needn't pre-build.<br>75.3 A full custom-interval builder stays **out of scope** (the app's model for arbitrary rides is post-hoc analysis) — noted, not built.<br>75.4 Tests (new subtypes expand to a valid multi-step IR at the right %; catalog listing includes them; copy renders) + gates. | Cover the common "a ride with some Z3 / some efforts" case in one tap, and make it obvious that anything truly bespoke can just be ridden and read afterwards. | The cycle quick-add offers tempo/Z3 and a VO2/efforts preset that deliver as real structured sessions (not a flat block); the post-hoc "just ride it" path is discoverable in the UI; no interval-builder scope creep; no migration; full gates; closeout smoke. Decision #148 (assigned at `/batch-start`). |

## Post-roadmap — 2026-07-10 workout-organiser feedback batch plan

Mark's follow-up 2026-07-10 note on organising workouts (the earlier 2026-07-10
note drove Batches 73–75): *"Tried adding a ride to today and changing time which
worked but when I went to skip it to get rid of it it cleared all cycling
including the workout I'd already done and checked in on so now thinks no cycling
at all today. … The workout part still seems a bit clunky / rigid. It also
doesn't seem to know about light reset week this week, holiday next week and
restart 13 week block 2 20/07. I have some ideas on this to make it more flexible
leave it with me."*

**Reconciled against the code (2026-07-10).** Two distinct things:

1. **A real data-loss bug.** "Skip day" is a *whole-day* action: `POST
   /api/v1/plan-actions/days/{date}/skip` → `skip_day` (`plan_actions.py:393`)
   skips **every** active session on the date via `_active_workouts_on`
   (`plan_actions.py:432`), whose filter is only `is_active AND status !=
   'skipped'` — it does **not** exclude `completed`. Completion sets
   `status='completed'` but leaves `is_active=True` (`workout_completion.py:75`),
   so a day-skip flips the already-ridden, checked-in session to `skipped` → "no
   cycling at all today." The Week tab makes this the *only* skip control
   (`WeekAheadPage.tsx:285`), so getting rid of one added ride there forces the
   whole-day nuke. Per-item `skip_workout` (`executable_coaching.py:771`) has the
   same missing guard — unlike `swap_day`, which already refuses to move a
   completed session (`executable_coaching.py:874`). A correctness fix,
   independent of the redesign → **Batch 76**.

2. **The "clunky / rigid / doesn't know about …" theme is mostly *surfacing*, not
   missing engines.** What Mark's asking for largely already exists, fragmented
   across separate screens the organiser knows nothing about:
   * **reset week** — the 13-week `BLOCK_SEQUENCE` is 2-build/1-recovery
     (`coaching_state.py:493`), so a "light reset week" *is* a `recovery` block;
     but the slate is auto-anchored to the seed Monday (`_current_cycle_start`,
     `coaching_state.py:21`) with **no control to say "this week is a deload,"** so
     it rarely lines up with his real life. *(The one genuinely-new piece.)*
   * **holiday** — a full pause/resume feature exists (`holiday_pause.py`, page
     `/holiday`) but lives on its own screen, disconnected from the organiser.
   * **restart block 2 on 20/07** — the Block Generator (`/builder`) already
     generates a fresh 13-week block **anchored to any start date** and locks it
     in; **verified** the lock cleanly supersedes the overlapping seeded plan by
     date-versioning (`block_generator.py:475`) — so this is *discoverability*,
     not a bug.

   Mark has said he wants to lead this redesign ("I have some ideas … leave it
   with me"). Since the engines exist and are correct, the remaining work is
   UX/design — surfacing deload/holiday/block-anchor *inside* the organiser plus
   the unifying "rearrange the whole week in one tap" restructure. **Held as
   design-pending below — not batched until his direction lands.**

**Scope chosen with Craig:** ship the data-loss bug now as **Batch 76**; hold the
flexibility redesign as a Mark-led design-pending item (candidate scope recorded
so nothing is lost).

bump `PROMPT_VERSION` (regenerates stale reads via the existing staleness check).<br>87.6 Frontend: the completed-ride / post-ride check-in becomes the **generate CTA** with a "reading your ride…" pending state over the LLM call, surfacing the returned read inline (`DashboardPage.tsx`); a Home affordance invites the check-in while a session is unread (mirror `GoodMorningCta.tsx`). **This is where "all four types" costs the most:** today only **rides** have a check-in form (the rich completed-ride logger + standalone post-ride check-in, `DashboardPage.tsx:317`/`:349`); strength/flexibility/walk **render** their read but have **no** check-in surface, so their (backend-supported) `activityCheckIn` is never written — so add a **minimal "how did it feel?" check-in** (RPE/feel/notes, posting to the same generic endpoint) for strength/flexibility/walk, rides keeping the richer logger. **Build-time dependency to confirm at `/batch-start`:** Batch 60's consolidated completed-*row* treatment was ride-scoped (strength/flex/walk completion was left as a fast-follow), so those reads may still render in a standalone analyses section rather than a Today row — confirm where the non-ride check-in attaches before building. **Decide at `/batch-start`:** button copy + whether generation is a **hard gate** on the check-in or keeps an explicit **"just read it now"** affordance (a finished ride is not a once-a-day event with a natural pause like waking — he may want the read on the spot).<br>87.7 Tests (sync-then-nudge ordering with no auto-generate on the primary poll; check-in submit generates inline and reflects notes; empty submit = objective read; the backstop still generates an un-checked-in session before morning; a question in the notes is answered; the nudge replaces the analysis-ready push on the primary path) + backend/shared/web gates. | Bring the post-workout loop into line with the Batch 85 morning **for every workout type (ride / strength / flexibility / walk)**: after a session the app pulls the data and invites a "how did it feel?" check-in, and his tap generates the read *from his input* — instead of auto-writing a read that ignores his input until a later poll (Mark's original "my typed input goes nowhere" complaint that motivated Batch 85). | A newly synced session syncs then nudges (no auto-generate on the primary poll); the post-ride check-in generates the read inline with RPE/feel/notes folded in; empty check-in = the objective read; the evening backstop still covers a session he never checks in on, before the next morning packet needs it; a question in the notes is answered; post-workout stays **read-only** (no delivery writes); `PROMPT_VERSION` bumped; **no migration** (confirm at `/batch-start`); verdict / #133 / #135 / Red-never-VO2 unchanged; full backend + web gates; closeout prod smoke on merge SHA **plus a live eyeball** (finish a ride → nudge → check-in tap generates a read reflecting the input — cannot be smoke-tested). Post-workout analog of the shipped Batch 85. **Scope resolved (Craig, 2026-07-11): all four post-workout types in one batch** (ride / strength / flexibility / walk — all run the same poll loop today). The check-in write endpoint + per-service consumption + staleness are **already generic across all four**, so the incremental cost of "all four" is the **inline-generate dispatch by type** (87.3) and a **minimal non-ride check-in surface** on the strength/flexibility/walk Today rows (87.6) — rides keep their richer logger. Decision #160 (assigned at `/batch-start`). |

**Now batched (2026-07-11, Mark's feedback — two items).** Mark reported (1) the
Morning Brief cutting off mid-sentence (screenshot ended on "*Yesterday's ride was
a*"), and (2) that ad-hoc questions he types into the check-in "Anything worth
noting" field go nowhere — the field is one-way context, and the brief is generated
at wake *before* he checks in (`scheduler.py:265`), so his input never reaches it.
Reconciled against the code with Craig and shaped into a "say good morning" redesign:
he initiates the brief from his check-in (data pre-synced so it's fast), it answers
any question in his notes, and it leads with a scannable actions-on-top format.
**Split into three by verification profile, not by topic** (they are one experience
but verify very differently, so they ship in dependency order): **84** truncation fix
(verifies in minutes; a live bug, so it ships first and de-risks the longer briefs
downstream), **85** the check-in-first reorder + answer-his-questions (backend +
prompt; needs a live-morning eyeball; the behavioural heart, proven before any UI
rides on it), **86** the hybrid actionable brief (structured "Today" actions +
tappable-to-approve; additive UI, landing last so Mark can react to the format and we
tune it). Root cause + reconciliation detail: truncation is `max_tokens`-driven
(`config.py:54` = `1600`) with no `stop_reason` guard in the shared Anthropic
boundary; the check-in note already reaches the packet (`manualEntries[].notes`) but
nothing regenerates the brief to answer it and the prompt has no "answer the question"
behaviour.

**Now scoped (2026-07-11, Craig — post-workout symmetry).** Craig asked to confirm
that every interaction follows one flow — pull data → offer a manual check-in → he
taps to generate the AI narrative — and whether that holds for the morning brief
(Batch 85/86) *and* every post-workout situation. Traced against the code: the
**morning matches** (wake fires `run_morning_sync` = sync + "good morning" nudge, no
LLM; the check-in force-regenerates the brief inline, `daily_loop.py:1184`; 09:30
backstop covers a skipped morning), but **post-workout is currently the reverse** —
the hourly `run_garmin_activity_poll` (`scheduler.py:546`) syncs the activity **and
auto-generates the read in the same loop** (`generate_for_pending_rides`
`post_workout_analysis.py:243`, + strength/flexibility/walk siblings), pushing
"analysis ready"; the post-ride check-in (`upsert_post_ride_checkin`
`daily_loop.py:1228`) only **saves** and leaves a **lagged next-poll regen**
(`_analysis_is_current`) to fold his input in. So his RPE/feel/notes never shape the
*first* read — the exact "my typed input goes nowhere" complaint that motivated
Batch 85, one loop over. Scoped as **Batch 87** — the post-workout analog of 85,
reusing 85's nudge/backstop/check-in-first machinery: split the poll's sync from
generate, nudge "how did it feel?" after sync, make the check-in the generate
trigger (inline `generate_and_store`), and add an **evening backstop** (must run
before the next morning packet consumes yesterday's ride read). Read-only path, so
no delivery-write guardrail and (likely) **no migration**. 🔴 High (poll seam +
prompt behaviour, like 85). Decision #160 reserved (assigned at `/batch-start`).
**Scope resolved (Craig, 2026-07-11): all four post-workout types** (ride /
strength / flexibility / walk) in one batch, not rides-first. The code makes this
cheaper than it first looked — the check-in **write endpoint**
(`upsert_post_ride_checkin`, keyed by `activity_id`) and **per-service
consumption** are already generic across all four (rides read `postRideCheckIn`;
strength/flexibility/walk read `activityCheckIn`, each with its own staleness
guard), so the only genuinely per-type work is (a) dispatching the **inline
generate** to the right service by activity type, and (b) adding a **minimal
check-in surface** for strength/flexibility/walk on their Today rows (today only
rides have a check-in form, so those types' `activityCheckIn` is never written).
**Open `/batch-start` calls:** (1) hard-gate generation on the check-in vs. keep a
"just read it now" affordance (a finished workout isn't a once-a-day event with a
natural pause like waking); (2) backstop time/threshold; (3) nudge + button copy.

## Post-roadmap — 2026-07-11 full-control workout editor batch plan

**Scoped 2026-07-11 with Craig — full control over a cycling workout on any given
day.** Craig wants Mark to be able to take full control of a ride's structure when he
chooses, beyond the Batch 77 builder's single interval-pair-or-block shape and the
Today-card's whole-workout duration/intensity scale (Mark already has the basic manual
edits; this is the whole canvas on demand). **Traced against the code — the delivery
format is *not* the limit:** `expand_structured_steps` (`services/workout_delivery.py:139`)
already expands an arbitrary-length ordered `steps` list (ramp / steady /
interval-pattern, any count, any order) into the IR that both the intervals.icu/Zwift
push (`reconcile_deliveries`) and the Batch 78 Garmin export already consume. The
single-pair-or-block ceiling lives only in the builder spec `CustomBikeWorkoutSpec`
(`services/structured_workout_builder.py`) and its UI — so "full control" is a builder +
UI change over the same rail Mark already uses, not a delivery rewrite, and the code that
actually talks to Zwift/Garmin is untouched. **Two decisions taken with Craig:**
(1) control level = **free-form segment builder** — add/reorder any number of segments,
each with its own duration + %FTP; (2) guardrails = **soft warnings** — on Mark's
explicit manual path the three gates (power 45–150% FTP, ramp-required, Red-never-VO2)
become non-blocking warnings, while the coach/automated authoring path keeps them
**hard**. The path-scoped soft-gating — and specifically making Red-never-VO2 a *warning*
on a workout Mark explicitly authored for himself (a deliberate, recorded reversal of the
long-held "Red-never-VO2 unchanged" invariant, scoped strictly to manual authoring) — is
the batch's central design point. Full spec:
`docs/designs/full-control-workout-editor.md`. Depends on the shipped Batch 77.

| Batch | Tier | Status | Phases | Goal | Acceptance criteria |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| ~~Batch 88 — Full-control free-form workout editor~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 88.1 Generalise the builder spec: replace the fixed-field `CustomBikeWorkoutSpec` (`services/structured_workout_builder.py`) with an **ordered list of segments** (`kind ∈ ramp/steady/interval`, each with its own duration + %FTP), reusing the exact per-kind step emission `build_custom_bike_workout` already does inline so any count/order authors the existing Batch 67 `steps` grammar; the `structured_workout` shape, `totalDurationMin`, and workout-type classification stay unchanged downstream.<br>88.2 **Path-scoped soft warnings:** on Mark's explicit manual authoring path only, the three delivery gates become warn-not-block — power outside 45–150% FTP (`_required_power`), no warm-up/cool-down ramp (`validate_deliverable_bike_workout`, `workout_delivery.py:178`), and VO2 on a Red-readiness day (Red-never-VO2 delivery gate). The coach/automated authoring path keeps all three **hard**. **Decide the mechanism at `/batch-start`** (spec flag vs. a separate manual-authoring validation entrypoint).<br>88.3 Warnings channel: the add/edit responses carry only hard `errors` today — add a `warnings: [...]` list so a **successful** save returns advisory messages the UI can surface. **Decide the contract at `/batch-start`.**<br>88.4 Frontend: a segment-list editor (add/remove/reorder rows, kind selector + fields) on the same Week-tab build + structured-edit surfaces Batch 77 shipped, surfacing warnings inline ("heads-up… deliver anyway") rather than blocking submit; a live power-profile preview + running total from the expanded IR (`powerStartPct/powerEndPct/durationSec`) so Mark sees the workout before it ships (**confirm in scope at `/batch-start`**).<br>88.5 Reuse the existing add (`customBike`) + structured-edit (`POST …/planned-workouts/{id}/structured`, `plan_actions.py:349`) endpoints so versioning, indoor Zwift re-sync, and outdoor Garmin routing carry over unchanged; completed workouts still cannot be structurally edited.<br>88.6 Tests (a many-segment free-form workout authors valid IR + delivers; segments in any order preserve order; each soft gate warns-not-blocks on the manual path but still hard-fails coach/automated authoring; the warnings channel surfaces on a successful save; structured edit versions + re-syncs) + backend/shared/web gates. | Let Mark take full control of a ride's structure on any given day — build an arbitrary multi-segment workout, warned but never blocked — over the same delivery rail he already uses. | A free-form multi-segment workout authors valid IR and delivers indoor→Zwift / outdoor→Garmin unchanged; segment order is preserved; on Mark's explicit manual path the power / ramp / Red-never-VO2 gates warn but don't block, while coach/automated authoring keeps them hard (proven by test); the `warnings` channel surfaces advisory messages on a successful save; structured edit still versions + re-syncs and completed workouts stay non-editable; **no migration** (segments serialize into the existing `structured_workout` `steps` — confirm at `/batch-start`); verdict / #133 / #135 unchanged; Red-never-VO2 stays hard everywhere **except** the explicit manual authoring path (Decision #161 records the scoped reversal); full backend/shared/web gates (Node 20); closeout prod smoke on merge SHA + a phone eyeball of the segment editor. Depends on Batch 77. Decision #161 (assigned at `/batch-start`). |

### Batch 89 — Enable RLS on the coach.* health-data tables

Surfaced by the 2026-07-11 full-app QA review (`QA_REVIEW_2026-07-11.md`, Finding 1).
The Supabase security advisor flags a **critical `rls_disabled`** lint: 18 of 23
`coach.*` tables (all of Mark's health data — `sleep`, `daily_metrics`,
`analyses`, `activities`, `manual_entries`, …) have Row Level Security **off**,
because only migration 001's five auth/notification tables were ever put under
RLS; every table added in 002-014 was left uncovered. This project's Postgres is
**shared with a separate public-facing movie app** whose anon key ships in its
frontend, which sharpens the concern. **Verified during scoping:** the `anon` and
`authenticated` roles hold **no grants** on the `coach` schema today, so nothing
is actually reachable via the Data API — the fix is **defense-in-depth**, not an
open breach. The backend connects as the `postgres` owner (bypasses RLS), so
enabling RLS with no policies is deny-all for `anon`/`authenticated` and leaves
the app untouched.

| Batch | Tier | Status | Phases | Goal | Acceptance criteria |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| ~~Batch 89 — Enable RLS on the coach.* tables~~ | 🟢 Mid | Shipped | 89.1 New migration `015_coach_rls.py` — `ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` on the 18 `coach` tables migration 001 left uncovered (the 17 remaining model tables + `alembic_version`), **no policies** (owner bypasses; `anon` has no grants → deny-all, matching `audit_log`). Table list kept as a `RLS_TABLES` constant. Downgrade disables. Wrapped in migration 001's exact `IF EXISTS (auth schema)` guard so it runs **only on Supabase** and is a no-op on plain Postgres (CI `migration-check` + unit-test Postgres stay green).<br>89.2 Regression test (`tests/test_coach_rls_migration.py`): 001's set ∪ 015's set == the coach model tables on `Base.metadata` — a future table shipping without RLS fails the test.<br>89.3 Correct `QA_REVIEW_2026-07-11.md` Finding 1 + STATUS open item (b) to the accurate exposure picture (data not currently reachable; RLS is the backstop). | Every `coach` table carries RLS as defense-in-depth, matching the auth tables from migration 001, so a future stray `GRANT` or exposed-schema change can never leak Mark's health data — and the Supabase critical advisor clears. | Migration enables RLS on the 18 tables on Supabase and is a guarded no-op on plain Postgres (CI `migration-check` upgrade→downgrade + pytest green); the app is unaffected (owner bypass); no policies added; regression test proves 001+015 cover every coach model table; **no schema/data change** beyond the RLS flag; verdict / #133 / #135 / Red-never-VO2 untouched; backend gates green; closeout prod smoke on merge SHA **plus a post-deploy Supabase advisor recheck** (the `rls_disabled` critical lint clears and the daily-loop still serves for Mark — RLS can't be smoke-tested from the app alone). Surfaced by the QA review. Decision #162 (assigned at `/batch-start`). |

## Post-roadmap — 2026-07-11 flexibility-read accuracy batch plan

Mark's 2026-07-11 note (two screenshots) after logging a mobility/stretch session:
"couple of errors in apps feedback." **Both screenshots are one `post_flexibility`
read** — the system prompt's shape is acknowledge → consistency → heart-rate →
*one light next step* (`post_flexibility_analysis.py:44`), and the "Advisory only —
this analysis does not inform recovery status or cycling session decisions" footer
is that prompt verbatim. Every sentence Mark flagged is **LLM-generated from the
context packet** (`assemble_flexibility_packet`, `post_flexibility_analysis.py:222`),
so each error is missing/stale packet data or a loose prompt, never a template
string. Root cause verified against the code:

1. **"today (Friday)" — wrong day.** The packet hands the model
   `subjectDate: "2026-07-11"` as a bare ISO string (`post_flexibility_analysis.py:241`)
   and **no weekday name**, so the model computed the day itself and got it wrong —
   11 Jul 2026 is a **Saturday**. This is latent everywhere: no packet builder (morning
   verdict or any `post_*`) emits a weekday string, so any read that names a day is
   guessing.
2. **"mobility on Mondays and Sundays … today's session is a bonus on top" /
   "volume on the fuller side."** Straight from the `training_plan` seed's `weeklyRhythm`
   (`coaching_state.py:148` — "Monday recovery or mobility strength" + "Sunday light
   strength or mobility"), fed to the packet as `trainingPlan`
   (`post_flexibility_analysis.py:251`). That rhythm is the **cycling-block scaffold**;
   it models mobility as a Mon/Sun add-on, not Mark's daily baseline. The data even
   contradicts it — consistency shows an 8-day streak and 6 mobility sessions this
   week (i.e. daily) — but the model anchored to the plan text over the behaviour.
3. **"a VO2 focus day (Tuesday) … let tomorrow be easy," blind to the holiday.**
   "Tuesday VO2 focus" is again just `weeklyRhythm[1]` (`coaching_state.py:150`), a
   generic template line — next Tuesday is **14 Jul, inside the holiday window Mark
   set**. Holiday awareness is absent from every analysis packet: a grep for "holiday"
   across morning + all `post_*` returns zero hits, and this packet loads only
   **today's** planned workouts (`workout_date == subject_date`,
   `post_flexibility_analysis.py:362`), never next week's — even though
   `HolidayPauseService` already stores the window (`get_active_window`,
   `holiday_pause.py:142`) and flips in-window workouts to `status='skipped'`
   (`holiday_pause.py:212`). So the read had no signal the week was off and invented a
   live VO2 Tuesday.
4. **Daily flexibility framed as overdoing it / a whole-day recovery call.** The
   numbers are right and mobility-only (`compute_flexibility_consistency`,
   `post_flexibility_analysis.py:133`); 6/week *is* the habit. The "fuller side / take
   tomorrow genuinely easy" reading comes from (2)'s stale 2×/week model plus a loose
   "one light next step" instruction (`post_flexibility_analysis.py:44`) with no
   guardrail that mobility is low-load baseline — so the model escalated to whole-day
   recovery advice that **contradicts the packet's own
   `guardrails.neverFeedsRecoveryDecision`** (`post_flexibility_analysis.py:271`) and
   the advisory-only footer. **Two adjacent latent bugs found while tracing:** the
   packet's `analysisRules` pulls `knowledge_base.get("analysis_rules", …)`
   (`post_flexibility_analysis.py:252`) — a section that is **never seeded** (real
   sections are `data_quality_rules` / `coaching_protocol`), so it is **always `{}`** in
   all four post_* reads; and the flexibility packet **omits `training_schedule`** (only
   the morning verdict pulls it, `morning_analysis.py:303`), the section whose
   "respect Mon/Fri rest" and "**describe an exception as an exception instead of
   rewriting the routine**" notes (`coaching_state.py:175`) directly temper this
   mis-framing.

Scope: **one batch** — all four threads live in the same packet + prompt
(`post_flexibility_analysis.py`), so splitting would churn one file four ways. It is
🔴 High (analysis-engine prompt + framing/reasoning). Because the prose is
LLM-generated, tests assert on **packet assembly + prompt inputs** via the fakeable
client (the Batch 6/8 pattern, #47), not on model text. Proposed Decision **#163**,
assigned at `/batch-start`. Full spec: this section (a short design doc can be added
at `/batch-start` if the 90.3 daily-mobility-modelling choice warrants one).

| Batch | Tier | Status | Phases | Goal | Acceptance criteria |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| ~~Batch 90 — Post-mobility read: right day, holiday-aware, daily-mobility-as-baseline~~ | 🔴 High | Shipped | 90.1 **Weekday: supply it, never let the model derive it.** Add an explicit `subjectWeekday` (`subject_date.strftime("%A")`) to the flexibility packet (`assemble_flexibility_packet`, `post_flexibility_analysis.py:238`) and an output rule that the model must use the supplied weekday and never compute the date. Fixes "today (Friday)" for a Saturday session. **Decide at `/batch-start`:** thread the same `subjectWeekday` through the other LLM reads (morning verdict, walk, strength, ride — none supply one today) so they can't make the same slip, or keep it flexibility-scoped now.<br>90.2 **Holiday awareness in the packet.** Load `HolidayPauseService.get_active_window` plus any window opening within the read's forward horizon and surface it (window dates + a "next week is a holiday" flag); add a prompt rule not to cite plan sessions (VO2 etc.) that fall inside a holiday window as live. **Decide at `/batch-start`:** holiday-window flag only vs. also pulling the next 7–14 days of planned workouts (already carrying `status='skipped'` from `holiday_pause.py:212`) so the near-future is data-driven, not template-driven.<br>90.3 **Stop reading daily mobility as plan overshoot or recovery load.** Reframe packet + prompt so the observed cadence (packet already computes `currentStreak`/`sessionsThisWeek`/`sessionsPerWeek4w`) is Mark's **baseline daily habit** and `weeklyRhythm` is the *cycling* scaffold only — not a mobility budget; kill the "bonus on top / fuller side" framing. The "one light next step" must stay **within mobility** and never issue a day/bike recovery verdict, honouring `guardrails.neverFeedsRecoveryDecision` (`post_flexibility_analysis.py:271`) + the advisory-only footer. **Decide at `/batch-start` (central design point)** where "daily mobility is baseline" lives: (a) prompt framing over the existing consistency signal [recommended — tightest, self-correcting, no KB re-seed]; (b) a durable KB fact shared by all reads (new `routine` line or folded into `training_schedule`); (c) rewrite the `training_plan.weeklyRhythm` seed (heaviest — KB re-seed + touches every read).<br>90.4 **Give the read the context it's missing + version bump.** Fix the always-empty `analysisRules` key (`post_flexibility_analysis.py:252` references the never-seeded `analysis_rules`; real sections are `data_quality_rules`/`coaching_protocol`) and add `training_schedule` to the packet (the "describe an exception, don't rewrite the routine" + Mon/Fri-rest notes reinforce 90.3). Bump `PROMPT_VERSION` (`post_flexibility_analysis.py:40`). **Decide at `/batch-start`:** fix the empty-`analysis_rules` key in the flexibility packet only, or in the identical spot in walk/strength/ride too (`post_walk_analysis.py:232`, `post_strength_analysis.py:231`, `post_workout_analysis.py:329`).<br>90.5 **Tests + gates.** Fakeable-client packet tests: the packet carries the correct `subjectWeekday` for a known Saturday date; an active/upcoming holiday window surfaces and a template VO2 day inside it is flagged/suppressed; the packet frames daily mobility as baseline (baseline flag/field present, no "exceeds plan") and now ships `training_schedule` + a non-empty rules block; the read stays advisory (no recovery-decision output rule). Backend pytest/ruff/mypy (+ any touched shared/web) green. | Make Mark's post-mobility read factually correct and correctly framed — right weekday, holiday-aware, and treating his daily flexibility as the baseline habit it is rather than plan overshoot or recovery-worthy load — without letting an advisory mobility read make whole-day recovery calls. | The flexibility packet supplies an explicit weekday and the read never miscomputes the day; holiday windows are visible so it never cites a plan session inside a holiday as live; daily mobility is framed as consistency-driven baseline, not as exceeding the plan or as fatigue load, and the "one light next step" stays within mobility and never issues a day/bike recovery verdict (honouring `neverFeedsRecoveryDecision` + the advisory-only footer); the packet no longer ships an always-empty `analysisRules` and includes `training_schedule`; `PROMPT_VERSION` bumped; **no migration** (packet/prompt/framing only — confirm at `/batch-start`); verdict / #133 / #135 / Red-never-VO2 untouched; full backend gates; closeout prod smoke on merge SHA **plus a phone eyeball** of the next real post-mobility read (correct weekday, holiday respected, no "bonus/overdoing" framing). Surfaced by Mark's 2026-07-11 feedback. Decision #163 (assigned at `/batch-start`). |

## Post-roadmap — 2026-07-12 Mark feedback batch plan

Mark's 2026-07-12 morning note flagged four issues in the day's morning brief. All
four were reproduced against the stored analysis + source data for
`subject_date = 2026-07-12` (user Mark, `coach` schema); the first-guess "phantom
subjective feel" was **disproved by the data** and re-scoped. Root causes, each
verified against code + the actual packet Mark saw:

1. **Sleep time an hour behind ("sleeping at 00:17" vs the real 01:17).** Stored
   `sleep_start_utc = 2026-07-12T00:17:34Z` is correct UTC (= 01:17 BST). The packet
   ships only `sleepStartUtc`/`sleepEndUtc` (`_sleep_packet`, `morning_analysis.py:759`;
   `_dt` appends "Z", `:1517`) and nothing — packet or prompt — converts to
   `Europe/London`, so the LLM prints the UTC clock verbatim. Invisible in winter
   (UTC==GMT), off by exactly 1h under BST. Profile timezone is correctly
   `Europe/London`, so this is purely a presentation gap in the read. Same family:
   one 08:30 regen mis-dated its header "13 July" — the model deriving the date
   instead of using `subjectDate`.
2. **Bedroom "peaked at 24.1°C overnight" — wrong window.** The verdict's thermal
   window is a fixed **18:00→08:00 local** (`_overnight_window_utc`,
   `morning_analysis.py:1504`), so `max()` grabs the **24.05°C reading at ~18:1x BST**
   — daytime, before the pre-cool, ~7h before sleep onset (01:17). The true
   asleep-period peak was **20.2°C**. The pre-cool low **18.64°C** *was* captured
   (`indoorLowC`) but only flagged `precool_target_missed` and buried under the bogus
   peak, so a night Mark cooled 24→18.6 read as "ran significantly too warm." The
   `/bedroom` chart uses a *different* window (**21:30→09:00**,
   `bedroom_overnight.night_window:49`), so the two surfaces already disagree.
3. **"Age average restless moments is 13" — a fabricated number.** `restless=47`; the
   packet shipped `ageAverage: 13` from a hard-coded `averages` table
   (`age_norms.py:130`). Although the metric is `descriptive_only=True`, the
   descriptive branch still emits `age_average` (`:428`), so the number leaks and the
   model states it. It contradicts the module's own docstring ("no defensible
   population band … shown for context only", `:28`) and Garmin's ≤5/hr guidance
   (~35/night is fine), making Mark's normal 47 look alarming.
4. **"Subjective feel 6" he didn't recognise giving — NOT a phantom.** The data shows
   Mark *did* set it: `manual_entries.subjective_score = 6`,
   `feel = "A bit more tired this morning"`. He tapped **"OK" (=6)** in the Batch 63
   "Overall" chips (`OVERALL_OPTIONS`, `CheckInPage.tsx:26`) but doesn't connect that
   to "subjective feel", and the brief threw the internal term "subjective feel 6 /
   subjectiveScore 6/10" back at him — jargon he never saw. Two real problems: the
   read leaks the internal 0–10 term (backend, 91.3), and the input isn't recognisable
   as the feel check (frontend, 94; design resolved with Craig 2026-07-12 — keep the
   one-tap word scale, never show the number, rename + surface).

**Sequencing.** 91/92/93 are independent, migration-free backend fixes; run 92 and 91
first (the trust-eroding wrong facts), then 93 (honesty). 94 is frontend and **lands
with or after 91** (94.3 needs 91.3's "OK" wording for the vocabulary to match
end-to-end). Tiers per #19: 91/92 High (analysis-engine prompt + verdict-adjacent
thermal correctness); 93/94 Mid (well-specified data fix / component work). The #4
split is deliberate — the prose leak (91.3) is deterministic and ships now; the
check-in UX (94) carries the design. Decision numbers assigned at `/batch-start` (next
free **#164**).

## Post-roadmap — 2026-07-12 walkthrough UX batch plan

On 2026-07-12 Craig drove the full reset "just woke up" flow through the PWA on
prod as Mark (data snapshotted + restored) and logged **13 UX/flow points**. All 13
were reconciled against code the same day — full findings, root causes, and
clickable refs live in [`WALKTHROUGH_FEEDBACK.md`](../WALKTHROUGH_FEEDBACK.md).
Unlike the Mark-note batches above (analysis-engine correctness), these are almost
all **front-of-app UX** — the morning Home, the check-in→brief flow, notifications,
and the fan/environment surface — plus one coaching-correctness item.

**Key structural finding.** Four Home points (2, 3, 9, 12) share one root: since
Batch 85 the pre-brief Home shows a "Say good morning" hero (`DashboardPage.tsx:662`),
but the action resolver (`homeActions.ts`) and section model (`homeSections.ts`)
have **no "brief not generated yet" concept** — so the action strip falls to "You're
all set" (`homeActions.ts:118`, contradicting the hero), the rest-day section model
auto-expands Last-night sleep (`homeSections.ts:39-44`), and nothing claims the top
slot for the check-in/unread brief. Batch 95 introduces that state once and the
cluster dissolves.

**Clustering → batches (95–102).** 95 pre-check-in Home state + check-in
discoverability (pts 2, 3, 4, 12); 96 brief lifecycle — unviewed surfacing + button
state (pts 8, 9); 97 passive generation — notify-when-ready + staged loader (pt 6);
98 rest-day/holiday-aware morning verdict (pt 7, **correctness**); 99 iOS
notification deep-link (pt 1); 100 multi-fan support + richer telemetry (pt 10); 101
dedicated Environment/Climate tab (pt 11); 102 presentation polish — personal status
line + "Tonight" data transparency (pts 5, 13).

**Sequencing.** 98 is the only 🔴 High (Mark is getting factually wrong rest-day
coaching) — run it first, independent backend. 95 → 96 → 97 is the natural Home/brief
chain (each builds on the prior's brief-state model); 99 lands with/before 97 so the
ready-push deep-links correctly. 100 → 101 (the tab needs the richer per-fan data).
102 is independent polish, anytime. **98 follows through the shipped Batch 90.2**
(holiday awareness added to the *flexibility* packet; 90's own notes flagged
threading the same treatment through the morning verdict). Tiers per #19: 98 High
(verdict correctness); the rest Mid (scoped frontend / feature work). Decision numbers
assigned at `/batch-start` (next free **#170**).

| Batch | Tier | Status | Phases | Goal | Acceptance criteria |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|

## Post-roadmap — 2026-07-13 walkthrough follow-up batch plan

On 2026-07-13 Craig ran a second prod walkthrough (13th reset to pre-check-in,
driven as Mark) — this time against the **just-shipped Batches 95–102** — and logged
8 points. All 8 reconciled against the current code (full write-up in
[`WALKTHROUGH_FEEDBACK.md`](../WALKTHROUGH_FEEDBACK.md), 2026-07-13 section). Most are
**follow-up gaps in the batches that just landed**, several in the exact code they
touched:

1. **Pre-brief Home shows the CTA twice.** Batch 95 fixed the "You're all set"
   contradiction by adding a `say-good-morning` rung (`homeActions.ts:95-96`), which
   now echoes the `GoodMorningCta` hero's "Say good morning" + "Get today's brief"
   (`GoodMorningCta.tsx:38,44`) — two prompts for one action.
2. **Last-night sleep still reachable pre-brief** — the `lastNight` section renders
   collapsed under "More detail" before a brief exists (Batch 95 only stopped the
   auto-expand).
3. **Sleep page ungated** — Batch 95.3 added the check-in CTA (`SleepPage.tsx:88`) but
   the overnight chart / tonight / bedroom stats still render pre-check-in.
4. **Overnight graph on both surfaces** — `OvernightChartCard` renders on
   `SleepPage.tsx:124` *and* `EnvironmentPage.tsx:75`; wanted Sleep-only, Climate
   current-only.
5. **No calendar** — the Sleep page is a `last-night`/`tonight` binary
   (`SleepPage.tsx:21-26`).
6. **No read-aloud** — no TTS anywhere.
7. **Walking base + breathwork mis-filed** — both render in the Today workout card
   (`DashboardPage.tsx:1044-1045`).
8. **Thermal subsystem ignores holiday** — `run_evening_sleep_nudge` (`scheduler.py:180`),
   `run_evening_monitoring_alerts` (`scheduler.py:200`) / `evaluate_thermal_alert`
   (`nudge_alerts.py:264`), and `run_fan_control` (`scheduler.py:975`) never consult
   `HolidayPauseService`; the 12th (a holiday) fired an evening_nudge (19:00) + a
   **critical** thermal_alert (20:45). Batch 98 made only the *morning verdict*
   holiday-aware.

**Sequencing.** 105 (holiday env) is the correctness item — Mark gets false critical
alerts and a fan cooling an empty room on holiday — run it first, independent backend,
sibling of Batch 98. 103 (pre-check-in gating) directly finishes Batch 95 and is the
biggest UX win. 104 (placement) + 107 (calendar) pair with the sleep/climate split. 106
(TTS) is independent. Tiers per #19: 105 High (thermal correctness); the rest Mid.
Decision numbers assigned at `/batch-start` (next free **#176**).

## Post-roadmap — 2026-07-14 walkthrough follow-up batch plan

The 13th walkthrough continued into the 14th (the reset-13th test rolled past BST
midnight), and Craig logged a further wave. All reconciled against current code — with
**Batches 95–107 now all shipped**, these are follow-up gaps in that just-landed work
(full write-up in [`WALKTHROUGH_FEEDBACK.md`](../WALKTHROUGH_FEEDBACK.md), 2026-07-14
section). Two need no batch:

- **"Generated for the 14th" is not a bug** — the clock rolled past midnight, so
  `_local_today` (`daily_loop.py:128`) correctly returned the 14th; the reset-13th
  test simply went stale.
- **"Remove last night from Climate" is already done** — Batch 104 removed
  `OvernightChartCard` from `EnvironmentPage`.

The rest → Batches 108–112:

1. **The pre-check-in gate swallowed the calendar** — Batch 103's `hasSleepAccess`
   (`SleepPage.tsx:105`) hides the whole page, including Batch 107's `SleepDateCalendar`
   (`:124/:128`), until today's check-in — so other dates aren't browsable pre-check-in.
2. **The calendar is expanded by default and shows sleep-only** for a past date
   (`SleepPage.tsx:133-168`), though `historyData` holds the whole day.
3. **Home `tonight`/`bedroom` ignore holiday** — Batch 105 gated only the backend
   scheduler; the frontend sections have no holiday awareness.
4. **Check-in flow leftovers** — the staged progress is a card below the form
   (`CheckInPage.tsx:405-453`) not in-place, and the inline brief render
   (`:456-473`) still duplicates what Home's `UnviewedBriefCta` now shows.
5. **Home says the verdict twice** — the lockup `personalStatusLine`+date
   (`DashboardPage.tsx:684-691`) duplicates `VerdictHero` (`:697`).
6. **Read-aloud is robotic** — Batch 106 shipped the default `SpeechSynthesis` voice.
7. **Stale/redundant notifications** — the critical thermal alert deep-links to the
   retired `/bedroom` route (`nudge_alerts.py:388`, now a redirect, `App.tsx:115`), and
   `verdict_push` (→`/`) overlaps `brief_ready_push` (→`/brief`) for the same brief.

**Sequencing.** 108 first — it's a regression (Batch 103's gate broke Batch 107's
calendar). 110 (brief-flow + verdict de-dup) is a quick UI cleanup. 109 completes Batch
105's holiday-awareness on the frontend. 112 is backend notification hygiene. 111 (voice)
hinges on the on-device-vs-hosted-TTS privacy call. Tiers per #19: all Mid (108's
calendar-gate is a regression fix, worth prioritising) — no 🔴 High this wave, since
Issue 12 turned out not to be a defect. Decision numbers assigned at `/batch-start` (next
free **#181**).

## Post-roadmap — 2026-07-14 walkthrough follow-up batch plan (wave 2)

A second 14th wave (the walkthrough continued through the morning). 13 points reconciled
against current code — **Batches 108–112 now shipped too** (full write-up in
[`WALKTHROUGH_FEEDBACK.md`](../WALKTHROUGH_FEEDBACK.md), 2026-07-14 wave 2 section). One is
already fixed and one is partial:

- **Fixed:** the check-in progress now replaces the button in place with no inline brief
  (Batch 110, `CheckInPage.tsx:378`) — that observation predated the fix.
- **Partial:** Batch 110 removed the duplicate *date* above the verdict, but the personable
  status line still doubles it (`DashboardPage.tsx:733`) → Batch 115.

The rest → Batches 113–119:

1. **Holiday still leaks thermal where the scheduler-only gate (105) didn't reach** — the
   brief's thermal review + "pre-cool" action (`morning_analysis.py:1202/1226`) and Sleep's
   Last-night fan chart (`SleepPage.tsx:194`) all still show on a holiday; and the pre-cool
   action links to `/sleep` instead of `/environment` (`:1222`).
2. **Check-in CTAs don't clear** — Home's hero gates on `analysis` not `manualEntry`
   (`DashboardPage.tsx:739`, so Batch 97's async window still nags), and Sleep's "Add today's
   check-in" card shows *because* `hasSleepAccess` is true after check-in (`SleepPage.tsx:286`).
3. **Home doubles the verdict/greeting** (`:733` above `:740`) and stacks "You're all set"
   (`:770`) against a Today card saying the same.
4. **Read-aloud is still robotic** — Batch 111 picked the best *on-device* voice
   (`BriefListenControls.tsx:60`); the natural voice needs the deferred hosted-TTS path.
5. **Calendar chevrons page by month** (`SleepDateCalendar.tsx:40`), not day.
6. **Feedback is only a 3-way rating** (`FeedbackControl.tsx`) — Mark wants more specific.
7. **No follow-up conversation** on a brief — it answers only the single check-in question.

**Sequencing.** 113 (holiday-thermal) and 114 (check-in CTAs) are the most user-visible daily
annoyances — do first. 115 (Home de-dup) is quick. 116 (hosted voice) and 119 (follow-up chat)
are the two heavier, decision-gated pieces (both carry a health-data choice — a third-party
voice API, a conversational surface). 117 (calendar day-nav) + 118 (feedback vocabulary) are
small. Tiers per #19: all Mid. Decision numbers assigned at `/batch-start` (next free **#186**).

Added `media-src 'self' blob:`. **Voice-quality reversion shipped (DECISIONS #197, bundled into PR #144's squash `9cb43d6` due to a `git checkout` race between two concurrent sessions sharing a working directory — see STATUS.md for the merge-mechanics note):** Craig heard the `low`-quality voice for the first time after the CSP fix and reported it "very robotic". A live `railway ssh` benchmark with realistic full-brief-length text showed `low` (23.27s) wasn't dramatically faster than `medium` (33.83s) — reverted to `en_GB-alan-medium`, timeout raised to 90s. Verified live in production (health SHA `dd1d048` matches `origin/main`, `config.py` confirms `en_GB-alan-medium`). **Still open:** whether the voice now sounds acceptable and completes within 90s for a real brief — needs one more live check with Craig. |

findings D1/P1–P7). Coverage is strong (14/16 user stories fully met, several
unusually well — verdict-first hero, the `copy.ts` plain-English system, one-tap
check-in); the gaps are in optimality, plus one real defect. Issues:

1. **Holiday self-contradiction (defect)** — on a live holiday morning the Brief
   ("Green — Rest Day (Holiday)", thermal omitted) and Sleep ("Holiday away", chart
   dormant, Batch 113) honour the holiday flag, but Home's Last-night sleep section
   still shows the live overnight room glance and the Climate tab shows the live room
   + active fan controls, and Home's hero reads "you're good to go tonight" (train
   framing, not rest). Home's `SleepSnapshotBody` renders `OvernightGlance` with
   `showOvernightGlance` defaulting true (`SleepSnapshotBody.tsx:26/40`);
   `EnvironmentPage.tsx` has no holiday gate; `personalStatusLine` (`copy.ts:55`)
   ignores rest/holiday.
2. **Metrics-vs-baselines lost its status column** — Mark named `Metric · Last night
   · Baseline · Status ✔/⚠` as the table he loves; `MetricComparisonTable.tsx`
   condensed it to 2 columns with the ✔/⚠ only on the age sub-line. The pattern he
   wants already exists on the same Sleep page in `SleepStageAgeTable` (`Stage · Last
   night · Healthy range · ✓/⚠`) and in the brief markdown's 4-column table.
3. **Home stacks too many prompts** — up to five attention blocks (feel recap,
   `FeedbackControl`, `UnviewedBriefCta`, `TodayActions`, `NextActionStrip`) between
   the verdict and the first section (`DashboardPage.tsx:757–789`); the amber "NEXT ·
   Review last night's sleep" button even duplicates the section right below it, and
   the daily rating ask sits under the verdict every morning.
4. **Coach memory is an internal panel, not Mark's** — the store meant to kill his
   handover doc is titled "Coach state", described as "the internal editor",
   admin-gated (showed "unavailable" for Mark on the live pass), and edited as raw
   JSON / plan-block / 13-week map (`CoachStatePage.tsx`). The thesis feature isn't
   Mark-facing.
5. **Sleep ⇄ Climate overlap** — the same 4-stat bedroom block renders on both Sleep's
   Tonight tab (`SleepPage.tsx`) and Climate (`EnvironmentPage.tsx`); the room chart
   lives on Sleep, the controls on Climate, a summary on both — users must learn where
   each fact lives.
6. **Week is an editor in a daily slot** — `WeekAheadPage` (titled "Plan") leads with a
   full editor (per-day add Cycle/Build ride/Weights/Flexibility, move/skip/remove/
   reset/restructure) in a primary tab for a user whose plan "won't change".
7. **Small type for a 57-year-old** — load-bearing readouts at 10–11px (the baseline
   "your normal" sub-line + "for your age" note in `MetricComparisonTable`, the verdict
   eyebrow in `VerdictHero`, the "More detail" label + mono eyebrows in `DashboardPage`).
8. **Presentation slips** — every analysis prompt self-titles "You are Garmin Coach"
   (`morning_analysis.py:83`, `post_workout_analysis.py:61`, `post_flexibility_analysis.py:48`,
   `brief_chat.py:52`) so the brief renders "Garmin Coach — <date>" inside a CheckMark
   shell; nav "Week" opens a page titled "Plan"; the bedroom fan surfaces its raw
   configured name ("Replacement 2 keeper").

Not batched: whether the check-in-gated verdict (no colour on a cold open until
check-in / the 09:30 backstop) matches Mark's "morning answer, always" expectation
(review P7) — a product question to confirm with Mark directly, not a build.

**Sequencing.** 121 (holiday consistency) is the correctness item — do first; the
holiday flag already reaches the client, so it's applying an existing gate to Home's
last-night glance + Climate + the hero line. 122 (status column) is the highest
"Mark will love it" win and reuses the in-house sleep-stage pattern. 123 (Home
de-stack) and 127 (type sizes) are quick frontend passes. 124 (Mark-facing coach
memory) is the largest — a new presentation layer plus a non-admin read — and 126
(right-size Week) both carry a `/batch-start` design decision. 125 (Sleep/Climate)
and 128 (presentation consistency) are small. Tiers per #19: all 🟢 Mid. Decision
numbers assigned at `/batch-start` (next free **#198**).

A fresh expert UI/UX walkthrough on synced `origin/main` (after 121-128 shipped),
rendering Home/Brief/Sleep/Climate/Week with realistic data. Two earlier findings
were already fixed by shipped work (Week redesign #152, Sleep⇄Climate overlap #151);
the items below are the gaps that survived. All 🟢 Mid, frontend-only, no migration.

  direction allow-list is incomplete (a good above-normal reading can render as a
  ⚠ warning), Climate repeats a single fan's status twice and prints
  "Mode unknown · Oscillation unknown", the workout subtitle leaks the raw enum
  ("Bike sweet spot"), tonight's prep actions use a "done"-style green check, and a
  couple of copy strings use developer jargon ("canonical", "rail one layer down").

  inside the Brief itself (Mark's stated favourite artifact, currently one tap away).
- **131** is design-pending — a longitudinal strength "watching-brief" (should he do
  more/less resistance work over time), his explicit ask that is still only partially
  met; needs a scope decision with Mark before building.

## Post-roadmap — 2026-07-16 rest-day activity surfacing batch plan

Traced from a live case — Mark's holiday walk on 16 Jul ("South Lakeland Walking",
70 min, on the last day of an active 12–16 Jul holiday window that had skipped his
Sweet Spot bike). The *treatment* is already correct and stays: the walk is captured
as an `Activity`, read as advisory active-recovery (`post_walk`, ≥30 min / 3 km via
`is_deliberate_walk`), never counts as load, never touches the skipped session, and
rolls into the Trends walking-base volume. What's wrong is *placement*:

- **Home (Batch 132)** — the walk lives only inside the Today card (`DayPlanBody` →
  `PendingWorkoutCheckIns` before its read generates, `WalkReadList` after), which on a
  rest day is collapsed under "More detail": the rest-day primary section is `lastNight`
  (`homeSections.ts:39`) and the `nextAction` ladder has a rung for an unlogged *ride*
  (`firstUnloggedRide`→`log-ride`, `homeActions.ts:112`) but **none for a walk** — even
  though the push nudge ("Your walk is synced — check in and I'll read it") already fired.
  **132** adds the missing walk rung so the walk floats to the top *while it's fresh*
  (decided 2026-07-16: dynamic, not a static re-rank of sleep), then recedes once seen.
- **Week/Plan (Batch 133)** — it doesn't appear at all: the plan-schedule
  (`planScheduleDaySchema`, `schemas.ts:404`) and week-ahead (`weekAheadEnvelopeSchema`,
  `schemas.ts:1238`) payloads are planned-workouts-only, so a day he actually walked
  renders as a blank rest day. **133** surfaces the day's synced activities on the day
  (decided 2026-07-16: shown on Mark's read-first Week glance, kind + duration).

Both prominence calls were made by Craig on 2026-07-16 (recorded in the rows below),
open to Mark's later feedback — same posture as Batch 131. Making the walk *more* visible
does not conflict with rest-day integrity: acknowledging an activity is not the same as
prompting training, and the advisory/no-load treatment is untouched. **132** is
frontend-only; **133** adds a read-only field to two existing endpoints (no new ingestion,
no migration). Decision numbers assigned at `/batch-start` (next free **#212**,
after Batch 134 takes **#211**).

| Batch | Tier | Status | Phases | Goal | Acceptance criteria |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| ~~Batch 132 — Surface the walk on a rest-day Home~~ | 🟢 Mid | Shipped | 132.1 Walk rung in the Home action ladder — `nextAction` (`homeActions.ts:90`) resolves a ride's unlogged check-in (`firstUnloggedRide`→`log-ride`, `sectionKey:'today'`) but has no walk equivalent; add a parallel rung (new `NextAction.key`, e.g. `read-walk`) that reads the already-present payload (`pendingPostWorkoutActivities` with `activityKind==='walk'`, and/or a fresh `postWalkAnalyses` entry) so a synced walk becomes the top Home action once the required morning sleep-review step is done, floating and expanding the Today card that holds it — mirroring the ride precedent and the push nudge that already fires — and clears once the walk is read/seen (server `pendingPostWorkoutActivities` empties when the read generates; a per-day 'seen' flag mirrors `hasReviewedSleep`/`hasReviewedBrief` for the generated read).
